Current Commentary

The Northwest Urgently Requires Attention

The conflict between Hui and Han peoples in Xinjiang has spread from the local area of Hami County to counties across the east, west, and south of the province. The Xinjiang provincial government has even relocated to avoid the conflict. The seriousness of the situation is acknowledged nationally. According to official sources, the cause of the incident stems from the Xinjiang provincial government's recruitment of White Russian soldiers, whose lax military discipline provoked resentment among the Hui people. Furthermore, the house arrest of the eight Hui princes led to national disunity. While these two factors may be somewhat abstract, we can recall Zhang Zongchang's recruitment of Russian soldiers; while his army was brave and skilled in battle, its poor discipline led to widespread resentment among the general population. Moreover, the Hui people have a particularly strong fighting spirit; how could they long endure violent oppression without resistance? Furthermore, the corruption of officials has not decreased compared to the Yang Zengxin era. How can one expect political stability in Xinjiang and reconciliation between the Hui people and the government?

Xinjiang covers an area of 5.36 million square kilometers, with a total population of only 3 million. From afar, it is almost seen as a desolate area, due to the vast Gobi Desert stretching across it and impeding transportation. In recent years, bandits and soldiers have roamed freely, making it a dangerous place. However, Xinjiang is rich in resources. In addition to precious minerals such as jade and gold, coal and iron ore are also abundant. Both the north and south of the Tianshan Mountains are rich in mineral deposits, and the richness of its coal and oil deposits is unparalleled within China. As for agricultural products, the areas along the Tarim River are all arable land. The reason for their lack of development is the sparse population and the fact that the general population is not accustomed to farming. As a result, goods are left on the ground, and people are content with a simple life, reminiscent of the primitive era. However, the province borders two major powers, Britain and Russia. If transportation were convenient, how could it not become a continuation of the three northeastern provinces? Taking the city of Kashgar as an example, one can see the active attention of foreigners, who are constantly watching from the sidelines, calculating how to make a move.

Recently, the three northeastern provinces have fallen, and Jehol, adjacent to the northeast, has also been seized by a powerful enemy, despite its inconvenient transportation. More recently, the strategic passes along the Great Wall have fallen into enemy hands, and the people of the five counties of Luandong are groaning under the iron heel. The impact on North China is significant, and the financial and economic impact on China as a whole is even greater. China's foreign trade, from the inland provinces to Tianjin, Shanghai, and Guangzhou, is characterized by imports exceeding exports. In other words, China is in a disadvantageous position in terms of trade balance. The three northeastern provinces are an exception, with exports exceeding imports for many years. Although Japanese financial and industrial investment there has exceeded 1.5 billion yen, the northeast remains rich and maintains its special advantageous position. Now that it has fallen, the prospect of its recovery is distant and uncertain. Before it is recovered, China's economic losses will be even greater than the loss of political power. The provinces of North China, such as Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, and Shaanxi, are all impoverished and await relief. It is difficult to use them as the vanguard for the recovery of the northeast, and it is not easy to supply them with provisions. Driving hungry people to war is something that has always been avoided. Moreover, in modern times, with the gradual awakening of popular wisdom, the people of the Republic are different from those of the autocratic era. Therefore, urgent, profound, and meticulous attention must be paid to the livelihood of the general population. Even if it is not possible to bear the burden of their lives individually, ways should be found to open up avenues for their livelihood, allowing them to flourish naturally. Only then will the country be able to become rich and its national strength gradually increase.

Therefore, for the sake of China today and for the sake of recovering lost territory, special attention should be paid to the northwest, with Xinjiang as the base and the Hetao area as the granary, so that there will be resources for food and supplies, and good land will be developed. The development of Wuyuan is a smooth process without great difficulties. It is only necessary to carefully select local officials and encourage them to be good officials, so that the general society gradually becomes orderly. Then the operation of collective farms can achieve the greatest results in the near future.

Before Xinjiang can be developed, there is still a prerequisite issue: the past malpractices must be reformed, and the divisions between ethnic groups must be removed. Otherwise, there can be no peace, and how can progress be achieved? China has always had no absolute prejudice against religion, and there are no problems between individuals. Therefore, there is no major conflict between Islam and the Han people in various parts of Xinjiang. As for the conflicts between ethnic groups, they mostly belong to disputes arising from politics. Such disputes can be easily resolved if politics are enlightened. Therefore, the development of the northwest cannot be delayed any longer, and new political measures are particularly urgent. When politics are on track, economic construction can begin. The vast fertile fields can not only accommodate tens of millions of immigrants, but also exploit its mineral resources and produce its agricultural products, which can be used as resources for recovering the lost territory in the northeast, and can also alleviate the poverty of the rural areas on the verge of bankruptcy in the interior and relieve the suffocating cities.

Discussion of Economic Difficulties

Anglo-American Talks Successful

Public Announcement Declares Five Points of Understanding Reached

Trade Restrictions Left for Conference Resolution

Roosevelt Meets Separately with Herriot

World Economic Conference Opens in Mid-June

(Washington) The Anglo-American talks in Washington are practically completed. The US President and the British Prime Minister jointly issued a statement today expressing deep satisfaction with the results of the discussion of difficult problems for the upcoming World Economic Conference. They also declared that the following points have been considered: (1) World commodity prices; (2) Central bank policies; (3) Currency standards; (4) Exchange rate restrictions; (5) Improvement of the silver standard. In addition, many difficult problems regarding world trade were explored, with emphasis on restrictive measures. However, the issue of restrictions will be left to the final decision of the World Economic Conference. The conference is expected to open in mid-June. (National Telegram from the 25th)

(Washington) Today, US President Roosevelt and British Prime Minister MacDonald jointly issued a public statement declaring that any agreements they have reached on economic or other matters will be temporarily withheld and disclosed at the World Economic Conference. They stated that they are deeply satisfied with the progress made. The issues discussed included the world commodity price level, central bank policies, currency standards, improving the position of silver, and various other issues related to world trade. (National Telegram from the 24th)

Franco-American Talks Begin

(Washington) In the evening, President Roosevelt received the French representative, former Prime Minister Herriot, at the White House. He led experts from both countries in talks lasting approximately three hours. Roosevelt presented the technical plan that the United States intends to propose at the World Economic Conference to Herriot. They then discussed the disarmament issue, and Herriot explained the reasons why France could not accept the MacDonald plan. Subsequently, the experts from both countries withdrew, and Roosevelt, Herriot, and French Ambassador de Laboulaye continued to discuss until 11:30 PM. Herriot left the White House and returned to the Mayflower Hotel at 11:40 PM and issued a statement saying that President Roosevelt clearly did not want the World Economic Conference to open in a chaotic situation, but wanted to create a complete plan. First, he wanted to negotiate a solution with France on a few clear points, and then obtain agreement from other countries. Experts from France and the United States are scheduled to meet again at the State Department tomorrow morning at 10:30 AM, chaired by Secretary of State Hull. French experts will begin studying the American technical plan tomorrow. The date for the second meeting between Herriot and Roosevelt has been set for Wednesday. (Havas Dispatch from the 24th)

(Washington) Although Undersecretary of State Phillips stated that the issue of war debts was not mentioned before the experts during the talks between French representative Herriot and President Roosevelt, the two may have discussed the matter. Herriot told the press that President Roosevelt's technical plan for the World Economic Conference has been handed over to economic experts for study to create a draft plan. (Havas Dispatch from the 24th)

Preparatory Committee for Economic Conference to Meet on Saturday

(London) The preparatory committee for the World Economic Conference will meet at the British Foreign Office on Saturday afternoon. Representatives from eight countries, including Britain, France, Italy, Germany, Japan, Belgium, Norway, and the United States, will attend. The US representative is Davis, the chief representative to the Disarmament Conference. This meeting will determine the opening date of the World Economic Conference. (Havas Dispatch from the 25th)

British and American Experts Continue to Discuss Equalizing Currency Prices

(Washington) British and American experts continued to discuss the key points of equalizing currency prices today. There are rumors that the two sides have different opinions on this issue, but the authorities deny it. It is reported that the discussion has not yet reached the stage of determining the ratio, but is focused on how to equalize currency prices and determine the best method. According to the authorities, the goal is not only to equalize currency prices, but also to focus on raising the general level of world commodity prices. (Reuters Dispatch from the 24th)

Suspension of Cash Redemption in Canada Is Tantamount to Abandoning the Gold Standard

The cabinet order to suspend the redemption of Canadian gold banknotes in Ottawa was passed today, but the implementation date has not yet been determined. Officials claim that this plan only adjusts the situation that has arisen since Britain abandoned the gold standard. (Reuters Dispatch from the 24th)

(New York) Wall Street bankers believe that Canada's suspension of cash redemption of gold banknotes is tantamount to a formal acknowledgment that Canada has abandoned the gold standard. It is expected that Canada's move will cause foreigners, especially American businesses, to withdraw their existing funds from Canada. If so, Canada's restrictions on gold exports will be tightened. Bankers here believe that Canada has already theoretically abolished the gold standard since Britain abandoned the gold standard in 1931. (Reuters Dispatch from the 24th)

(Washington) There was great panic here tonight when the Canadian Minister of Finance announced that the Canadian government had suspended the redemption of Dominion banknotes with gold. However, because the news arrived late in the US, it did not affect the gold dollar exchange rate today. The initial interpretation here is that it is a divorce movement between the Canadian dollar and the US dollar, as the two countries' dollars have had a close relationship for hundreds of years. Sometimes the Canadian dollar has suffered as a result. There may be a movement to make the Canadian dollar more closely tied to the gold pound. However, some financial experts believe that the Canadian government's move is necessary to stabilize international exchange rates. (National Telegram from the 24th)

The Momentum of the Inflation Movement in Congress Suddenly Declines

(Washington) Today, the momentum of the inflation movement in the US Congress suddenly declined. The silver faction has decided to delay all monetary reform bills pending further appeal by the President. The reason for this is not yet clear. It is reported that the Democratic leaders in both houses believe that the President and British Prime Minister MacDonald will be able to negotiate a satisfactory understanding, and that a similar understanding will be reached with former French Prime Minister Herriot. However, the White House and the experts who have met with Secretary of State Hull have not indicated that silver will be discussed separately. The silver faction in the Senate is unwilling to speculate on the outcome of the President's talks with foreign envoys. Other senators have suggested that the silver faction may have been misled, believing that the President is actually an advocate of sound money and that his request for the power to mint silver coins and inflate the gold dollar is only intended to prevent Congress from acting rashly. With the President in control, he can restrict inflation as he sees fit. One senator said that the President is clearly pretending to be in favor of inflating the currency in order to avoid a fierce debate in Congress when he and the heads of other countries work together to stabilize the currency. However, there is also an indication that the United States was forced to abandon the gold standard, revealing a situation that has caused members of Congress to postpone their original plans. This morning, British Prime Minister MacDonald and his daughter attended a breakfast at the home of Senator Borah, the leader of the silver faction and former chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, and then continued talks with the US President. Financial experts and economists are also still meeting as before. (National Telegram from the 24th)

Republicans Oppose the Currency Inflation Bill

(Washington) The Senate convened to discuss the currency inflation bill. Senator Thomas began his speech, saying that no bill submitted by parliaments around the world is as important as this one. There are 20 million US dollars in the hands of certain classes, and these classes did not obtain it through legitimate work. On the contrary, there is a class in debt that has the right to obtain this huge sum. The effect of the proposed bill is to transfer this huge sum from the former to the latter. The wording of this bill can make bank depositors and holders of interest-bearing securities transfer this money to the public. Republican Senator Little asked, "Is what you are saying the content of the currency inflation amendment?" Thomas replied, "(If it is not handled in this way, the indebted class cannot fully obtain justice)." When the discussion began, Senator Fletcher, chairman of the Senate Banking Committee, declared that he had originally opposed the devaluation of the US dollar clause, but is now prepared to support it. Senator Tydings, a Democrat from Maryland, echoed the Republican opposition to the currency inflation bill, saying that if this bill is passed, the United States will lose foreign markets, and at least 4.8 million people will lose their jobs. Although Republicans and some Democratic members of Congress strongly opposed it, the Senate seems likely to pass the bill within the next day or two. (Havas Dispatch from the 24th)

British Financial Circles Believe Currency Price Stabilization Is Impossible

(London) London financial circles believe today that the early stabilization of the British pound and the US dollar is impossible, as the appropriate parity depends on various factors, which are still unknown. However, Anglo-American talks do seem to have resolved many differences in principle. The fact that yesterday's joint communiqué from the US President and the British Prime Minister did not mention war debts is seen as noteworthy, but it is expected that the US President will continue to make statements on this matter within a week. Japanese Business and Industrial Groups Oppose Abolition of the Indo-Japanese Commercial Treaty

The Japanese Also Recognize Humanity and International Justice

Loudly Appeal to the British Indian Government

The newly formed Indian Affairs Economic Federation in Osaka passed the following resolution today: "The act of abolishing the Indo-Japanese Commercial Treaty disregards the friendship that has existed between Britain and Japan for many years, destroys the economic relations between India and Japan, and endangers millions of Japanese people who are engaged in the export trade to India. It only benefits a small number of industrialists in England and India, and what they gain is at the expense of 35 million Indians. In terms of humanity and international justice, this is intolerable. Therefore, all related associations oppose the abolition of the treaty and will consider effective countermeasures." The federation has representatives from 50 of the most important commercial associations in western Japan, including chambers of commerce and industry associations in Osaka, Kobe, and Kyoto. (Reuters Dispatch from the 25th)

Soviet Russia Denies Joint Ownership of the Chinese Eastern Railway

Li Shaogeng Publishes Letter

(Harbin) Koshnitsov, the Soviet General Representative of the Chinese Eastern Railway, responded to Li Shaogeng with a letter strongly refuting the claim that the Chinese Eastern Railway is jointly owned by Russia and Manchuria. He stated, "The Chinese Eastern Railway is a Soviet industry, only jointly managed. You know this well and need no further explanation." He then cited evidence contained in a previous document from the Russian Consul-General in Harbin regarding the ownership of locomotives and freight cars, and pointed out that Li Shaogeng and other officials have never adopted a positive plan to protect the interests of the railway, and there is no guarantee for the safety of railway employees and their property. Finally, he demanded that immediate measures be taken to address the above issues and issued instructions to the authorities in Manchuria not to interfere with the Chinese Eastern Railway and its connecting Eurasian transport and intermodal transport with railways in Russia, and requested that a situation be created so that the Chinese Eastern Railway can operate as usual. (Reuters Dispatch from the 25th)

(Harbin) Li Shaogeng's reply to Koshnitsov, the Soviet General Representative of the Chinese Eastern Railway on April 22 regarding the Chinese Eastern Railway train dispute, was published today. The content stated that the Soviet Union's claim that the Chinese Eastern Railway belongs to the Soviet Union has no legal basis, and denied that the Chinese Eastern Railway ever used 2,000 Soviet freight cars. He also said that the vehicles removed by the Soviet Union have not been returned due to the war. If Koshnitsov wishes to restore the Chinese Eastern Railway to its normal state, he must return all the freight cars and locomotives that illegally entered Russian territory before May 10. (Reuters Dispatch from the 25th)

(Harbin) The Soviet Federal Customs office in Pokranichnaya was blocked today and notified (Manchukuo) that the Soviet Federal Customs office in Pokranichnaya would cease inspecting all goods from today and that inspections would be conducted in Grodekovo.

League of Nations Resident Representative in China, Rajchman, Discusses Mission to China

Assisting in Construction Projects and Investigating Financial Issues

Departed Beiping Yesterday to Enter Nanjing and Will Visit Various Leaders to Negotiate

(Beiping) At noon on the 25th, our correspondent visited Rajchman, the League of Nations Resident Representative in China, at the French Embassy to inquire about the following issues: (Q) What is the mission of your assignment to China? (A) The League of Nations, at the request of your government's Minister of Finance, Song Ziwen, sent me as the Resident Representative in China. As for the mission, there are two objectives: (1) Because the League of Nations has sent many experts to your country, this trip is to discuss with your government how to jointly undertake construction projects. (2) To investigate your country's financial problems in order to engage in construction, and at the same time assist your government in its international publicity efforts. (Q) How long will you stay in China, when will you go to Nanjing, and what work do you plan to do in Nanjing? (A) After staying in your country for five or six months, I will return to Geneva. I am leaving for Nanjing this afternoon (the 25th). I have previously consulted with some of your country's leaders and have a very good impression of them. Your country's achievements are also excellent. After going to Nanjing, in addition to consulting with your country's leaders, I will continue to investigate financial problems. As for future itineraries, they have not yet been determined. (Q) Is there any hope for a recent meeting of the League of Nations Advisory Committee? (A) I have already sent a letter inquiring, but have not yet received a reply. (Q) Since the League of Nations recognizes Japan as an aggressor nation, should economic sanctions be imposed according to the League of Nations Covenant? Does the League of Nations have this determination? (A) This issue is being studied, and there are no concrete measures at present. (Q) Japan has announced that it will only fulfill its obligation to pay membership dues to the League of Nations and no other obligations. What countermeasures will the League of Nations take? (A) I am not very clear about this issue and cannot answer. (Q) What are your thoughts on the Japanese military's attacks in eastern Liaoning and along the Great Wall? (A) I have not studied it and have no opinion. (Q) Will the Sino-Japanese issue be discussed at the upcoming World Economic Conference? (A) Perhaps it will be discussed, but I am not sure. (Central News Agency, 25th)

British Chancellor of the Exchequer, Chamberlain, Explains the Budget to Parliament

War Debt to the United States Not Included, Striving for Balance of Revenue and Expenditure

Hoping the Washington Conference Will Promote the Restoration of Credit

(London) Reuters, 25th. At 3:20 PM today, the House of Commons convened. Every seat in the chamber and the visitors' gallery was filled. Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain rose to present the budget. Cheers erupted from the cabinet members' seats. After the cheers subsided, everyone listened attentively to Chamberlain's speech. He stated that the previous year's final accounts showed a shortfall of £32,679,000. As of March 31st, the national debt totaled £7,645,000,000, of which £897,534,000 was owed to the United States. War debts owed by various autonomous regions and colonies totaled £114,234,000. Debts owed to England by the Allied countries totaled £1,115,738,000, of which £755,875,000 was in French currency. The unreturned debts of Russia totaled £1,100,000,000. The shortfall in the budget included approximately £29,000,000 for repayment to the United States and a debt repayment fund of £17,000,000. Last year, total debt repayment required a net amount of approximately £15,000,000. Excluding the US debt, the net surplus exceeded £11,000,000, the result of which was even more satisfying than the surplus obtained in normal prosperous years. Last year's beer tax revenue totaled £74,000,000, the lowest figure in thirteen years. Customs duties and excise taxes decreased by £12,000,000. The exchange of bonds can obtain permanent benefits, but it cannot succeed unless we firmly adhere to a balanced budget. Last year's shortfall was due to the £29,000,000 repayment of the US debt. This year's budget did not include the repayment of the US debt or the payment of debts owed to England. Last year was a year of very good financial performance. England's achievements have aroused general praise. Income tax and surcharges decreased by £19,000,000 due to the substantial decrease in personal income. This year, England should repay the United States £51,000,000, while the compensation and debt returned by the Allied countries totaled £64,500,000. Chamberlain predicted that the revenue from beer and other beverage license taxes would decrease again. Chamberlain believed that the disputes between England and Ireland showed no signs of ending in the near future. Based on existing tax revenues, Chamberlain estimated revenue at £712,000,000. He also stated that the exchange rate equalization fund had been tested in turbulent times and was sufficient to maintain the exchange rate in a relatively stable position. The rumor that England used this fund to lower the price of the pound was not true. However, the amount was still insufficient, so he planned to ask the House of Commons to increase it. Chamberlain went on to mention the Washington talks, saying that he understood Roosevelt's move to suspend the gold standard was not made for negotiations with other countries, but was purely prompted by domestic circumstances. However, the current situation is indeed worrying. He hoped that the other plans proposed by the US President would definitely promote the restoration of trust. The English people's purchasing and saving power can still be maintained, not greatly reduced due to the sluggishness of international trade and the large number of unemployed. Chamberlain then announced that starting from January 1st next year, heavy vehicle taxes would be increased, and heavy oil would be taxed one penny per gallon.

US Naval Operations Director Ballard Retires

Replaced by Standley

(Havas) Washington, 24th. Secretary of the Navy Swanson has appointed Vice Admiral Standley as the Director of Naval Operations, replacing Ballard. Ballard has reached retirement age, but will not relinquish the position until after the end of the arms reduction conference. The Deputy Director will be Vice Admiral Sells, who has been appointed as Commander of the US Fleet and promoted to the rank of Admiral, replacing Admiral Leahy.

Anglo-Danish Trade Agreement Signed

Reuters, London, 24th. The first trade agreement of Great Britain since the Ottawa Conference of last year was signed today by Great Britain and Denmark. The agreement has been under negotiation for four months and has now been successfully concluded. Great Britain is presently negotiating trade agreements with the Scandinavian countries and Argentina. The terms of the Anglo-Danish agreement will be published in the near future. It is generally believed that Denmark has agreed to import 75 percent of its annual coal from Great Britain, and the British steel industry has also gained considerable benefit.

France's Policy of Peace

(Havas) Paris, 24th. Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour spoke at a rally in the Saint-Dié constituency, showing little concern for the recent panic in public opinion. He said that France had never let go of any opportunity to build peace. He would protect the security of his country carefully. If France did not obtain equal security internationally, the security of France itself would never be relinquished. Paul-Boncour also said that the various principles advocated in the French disarmament proposal had been approved by the majority of countries at the Geneva Disarmament Conference, and a portion of them had been adopted by the British proposal. Paul-Boncour further explained France's views on the Four-Power Pact plan, saying that its outline was nothing more than (1) seeking opportunities to prevent European countries from being divided into two opposing factions, maintaining and consolidating peace, and not allowing anyone to undermine it; (2) bringing France and Italy closer together, without loosening the relationship between the two countries created by the memorial of the European war and common interests. The justice of France's views can be seen from the recent debate in the British House of Commons. Paul-Boncour concluded by saying that although this task felt difficult, it was not impossible to accomplish.

Disarmament Conference Opens

National News Agency, Geneva, 24th. The Disarmament Conference is scheduled to open tomorrow afternoon. Representatives from several countries have already arrived here. German representative Nadolny met with representatives from Italy, England, and the United States, and with the conference chairman, Henderson, to discuss the procedures for the conference. The committee will first discuss the security part of the British disarmament plan.

Henderson Receives Peace Prize

Reuters, The Hague, 25th. The Carnegie Foundation today awarded a prize of £2,200 to Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson in recognition of his efforts to promote peace, and praised his perseverance, talent, and impartiality in the proceedings of the conference.

Political Situation on the Eve of a Gathering Storm

Political Association Advocates for the Formation of a Cabinet of Talents

Opposes Saito's Disruption of Constitutional Norms

Dentsu, Tokyo, 25th – Premier Saito has declared his determination to reorganize the cabinet, and the Seiyukai (政友會) has decided to end internal discord and proceed towards opposing the Saito cabinet. The Seiyukai believes that after the May 15th Incident (五一五事件) reached a certain conclusion and the extraordinary situation was resolved, the Saito cabinet should have relinquished power and returned to the normal path of constitutional government. Regarding the extraordinary international situation after the Manchurian Incident (滿洲事變), which cannot be resolved in a few years, the Seiyukai believes that a Seiyukai cabinet with an absolute majority of 300 members in the parliament should take charge of this kind of extraordinary situation. Based on this view, even if Finance Minister Takahashi resigns, the government's negotiations with the Seiyukai to supplement a successor will be decisively rejected. When the Finance Minister's resignation is realized, the Minister of Railways, Minister of Education Hatoyama, and other party cabinet members will inevitably advance and retreat together with the Finance Minister. The Seiyukai recognizes the extraordinary situation and advocates for the emergence of a cabinet of talents. If the current government opposes this return to constitutional norms and dissolves the parliament, the Seiyukai will not hesitate. All responsibilities for the resulting political turmoil should be borne by the government. It has been internally decided to adopt this stance and take a tough attitude towards the government.

China United News Agency, Tokyo, 25th – The Seiyukai has heard that Premier Saito is unwilling to relinquish power in the shortest period. Internal unrest within the party is gradually increasing. Seiyukai President Suzuki dispatched Secretary-General Yamaguchi today to visit the Minister of Railways, Tsuchiya, to inquire about the Finance Minister's true intentions and the actual situation of the political situation, and to ask Tsuchiya about his views on the cabinet reorganization, in order to determine a strategy of war or peace. After Yamaguchi met with Tsuchiya, he reported everything to Suzuki.

Earthquake in the Aegean Island

Reuters, Athens, 25th – A violent earthquake occurred on Sunday on the island of Kos (柯斯島) in the Aegean Sea, southwest of Asia Minor. There have been many deaths and injuries, and much material damage. According to a telegram from the island today, 74 people have died and more than 400 have been injured. The old town of Kos has been completely destroyed. Rescue teams are still searching for bodies in the rubble. The authorities have taken measures to provide housing and food for the victims. The island has a population of approximately 16,000 people.

Japanese Believe in Immortality, Researching Qin Shi Huang's Elixir of Life

According to the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun on the 21st, Qin Shi Huang sent Xu Fu to the eastern Penglai Islands (Japan) to seek the elixir of immortality. At that time, Xu Fu brought 500 young boys and girls, sailed across the ocean to Japan, and brought hundreds of ancient documents. After painstaking research, he invented the elixir of immortality. This medicine is now being researched by Mr. Moriichi Tsuchida of the Brewing Department of the Faculty of Engineering at Osaka University. Its ingredients are known to be a precise blend of (1) ginseng, (2) cloves, (3) fennel, (4) chilam, (5) Angelica japonica, (6) rhubarb, and (7) Ligusticum chuanxiong, with fermented substances, to become a kind of spiritual wine. Tsuchida has collected the materials for each medicine and is trying to brew it in the brewing experiment laboratory of the Faculty of Engineering using special equipment. As a result, he has created a strange and fragrant medicinal wine, which has attracted attention from all sectors of society.

National News, Warsaw, 24th – According to a report from Moscow, Lenin's corpse is visibly decaying, so his mausoleum is now closed to the public. After Lenin's death, experts applied medicine and placed him in a glass tube for people to pay their respects. The Soviet Russian government has now organized a committee of famous doctors and chemists to study the cause of the decay and how to prevent it.

Inspection Record of the Saho Bridge Area (Special Correspondent Geng Ya of this Newspaper)

Special dispatch from Santunying: Since the war in the East has gradually been losing ground, and the enemy forces have been increasing the number of Mongolian and Korean fresh troops, intensifying their offensive against the Xifengkou front, there have been fierce battles with gains and losses in the positions around the north and south of Saho Bridge (撒河橋) and Tuanting (團汀). After the reporter obtained the permission of Commander Zhang of the 38th Division of the 29th Army, a staff officer of the division was specially dispatched to guide me to inspect the front line. Fearing air raids, we set off from Zunhua at night. This section of transportation was also mostly carried out at night. The car passed through the East Gate, which was already closed, but after explaining the situation, we were allowed to pass. There were patrol sentries near the villages we encountered along the way, in groups of three or five, carrying guns and remaining vigilant. The car was also carrying more than a dozen boxes of guns and ammunition, and six machine guns. The road was rugged and bumpy, and we were deeply concerned that the ammunition would explode due to friction. Later, we gradually unloaded the guns and ammunition at a certain brigade headquarters and a certain regiment headquarters, and my heart was at ease. It was already midnight, and everything was silent except for the rattling of the car and the buzzing sound of the wind blowing through the power lines. The car's headlights suddenly revealed a red swastika flag waving as a marker. There were seven or eight large cars, each carrying the coffins of fallen soldiers, left on the side of the road to give way. Upon arriving at the office of the Red Swastika Society west of Santunying City, I saw a heavy truck with corpses underneath and wounded soldiers sitting on top. The scene was desolate and tragic beyond description, but one can imagine the intensity of the fighting on the front lines and the lack of transportation vehicles. The next morning, I met with Li Wentian, the Chief of Staff of the 38th Division, and heard about the course of the battle and the determination he held. He said, in brief: "Since the September 18th Incident (九一八事變) broke out and the three northeastern provinces were lost, this spring Japan only used three divisions and one mixed brigade to re-occupy our Rehe in less than six days. The nation is ashamed, and the soldiers are even more ashamed. Our army has been unable to reorganize since the 19th year of the Republic, and there are many deficiencies, but in terms of education, we have always taught the soldiers about righteousness. From now on, we will focus on external threats and not internal conflicts. The small results we have achieved are based on this. In the age of iron, the Great Wall, where one man could hold the pass and ten thousand could not pass, has lost its effectiveness. It is said that the attacker always wins and the defender always loses. Our army took over the defense hastily, the fortifications were not prepared, and the weapons are far inferior to those of the enemy. In every battle, we fight the enemy's sharp weapons with our flesh and blood. The magnitude of the sacrifice is hard to describe in a single word. But I hope that the government will make a major decision as soon as possible, and the people will strive to provide support. The country's future may not be hopeless." Just then, we heard the sound of a bell, which was used by the watchmen on our city to warn that enemy planes had arrived. We took shelter in a cave and saw six enemy planes, in two rows, flying over Zunhua, Jixian, Yutian, Luowenyu and other places for reconnaissance. Fortunately, they did not drop bombs, but the faces of the old people in the crowded cave had turned pale. Later, I took a car to the Saho Bridge position to see our army strictly guarding the west bank of the Luo River and the Yanjianshan and other highlands, which are within the effective firing range of the enemy's artillery. The houses and people were bombed by enemy planes and artillery shells even more fiercely than in Santunying. The bombs dropped by enemy planes were mostly marked with the words "special weight" (特重), as long as a person, weighing over 120 pounds, and capable of penetrating the ground to a depth of seven or eight feet, digging a hole as deep as a giant pool. People who had taken shelter in nearby caves were buried by the flying dirt, or crushed by the earth, resulting in countless deaths. Luowenyu and other places were also subjected to the horrific disaster of enemy aircraft bombing with (killing effect) and explosion bombs (destructive effect). In the areas not yet captured, the Japanese used absurd leaflets to confuse our ignorant people, and in the areas already trampled by the enemy's iron hooves, they even fantasized and pasted various paintings all over the walls. The reporter uncovered four of them: one depicts five people with their arms intertwined, one in the middle with a long braid, and the other two each holding the puppet state flag of Manchuria, stepping on the puppet state territory of "Great Manchuria" composed of (Jilin Province) (Fengtian Province) Heilongjiang Province (Rehe Province) (Xingan Province), with a large sun half-exposed behind them. The second picture is a picture of peaceful scenery, still adorned with puppet flags, suns, and happy red and green men and women, with the inscription: "The Manchukuo is a paradise that we never dreamed of. The five grains are abundant, the livestock are fat, under the rule of the Wangdao, all people live in peace and work in joy, in the age of Yao and Shun, there is a great atmosphere of peace." The third picture depicts Japanese soldiers buying things from our merchants, with the inscription: "The Japanese soldiers are all good family children, serving as soldiers for the country and for peace. They are very strict with troublemakers, but they are very reasonable with merchants and civilians, so the Japanese army is welcomed everywhere." The fourth picture is half a picture of a fairy scattering flowers, with the inscription: "People who are happy to follow the Manchukuo will enjoy happiness like this in the afterlife," and half a picture of King Yama judging cases, with the image of two criminals kneeling on the ground tied up, reflecting the pattern of the Big Sword Society killing each other in the karmic mirror, and King Yama being furious, ordering the ghost king to inflict various cruel tortures in hell, with the inscription: "People who betray the Manchukuo will suffer like this in the afterlife." Their contempt for our nation, still treating us as ignorant and ignorant slaves in the age of divine authority, can be described as the ultimate in insult and absurdity. Seeing this, no one can help but be infuriated. However, some of our ignorant villagers have been confused. For example, Zhang Fushun, a resident of Sanying, was originally a scout in our army, but later went to work outside the customs and was bought by the Japanese, revealing all of our military intelligence. He was caught yesterday, and he confessed immediately. He was very thirsty and asked two orderlies for water, but the soldiers, only thirteen or fourteen years old, shouted loudly, "Traitor, slave of a subjugated country, you still want to drink water?" He replied, "Who wants to be a slave of a subjugated country? I was really deceived by the Japanese." Hearing this, I felt pity for him. When the Manchu children living in the Shimenzhen Eastern Tombs were asked, "Are you afraid when the Japanese soldiers come here?", they always answered calmly, "No, we are Manchus." From this, it can be seen that the people in the war zone urgently need propaganda, so that they know the great righteousness of patriotism. Even if we embrace Buddhism at the last minute, it should not be delayed. The Japanese army not only has new and sharp weapons, but also clothing that adapts to the environment and is added at any time. Our Big Sword Society has repeatedly achieved success in close combat, so the enemy's vanguards are equipped with steel collars, vests, and helmets to protect themselves. Recently, in the battle on the river, they had rubber clothing that could be used for wading. However, because the clothing was too elaborate, their actions were clumsy. In a mountain in the Kou Nei, an enemy cavalryman was taking pictures from a high place, but was unexpectedly chased by our army. They were frightened and did not have time to ride their horses, and were burdened by their heavy clothing and leather boots, which made it difficult to run, so they were captured by our sentries. The soldiers were awarded 200 yuan for capturing the prisoners alive, but the soldiers all said that capturing prisoners alive was great, but it was troublesome to escort and guard them, and if they escaped, the enemy would have one more person's firepower, so the soldiers considered this a big burden. The residents of Santunying were originally very poor, and with the continuous bombing of the Japanese aircraft, the scene was even more desolate. However, in the wilderness of smoke and grass, the stele of Qi Jiguang's words and the tombstone of Xueyan still stand tall, providing a place for future generations to mourn. The Jingzhongshan Beijige Temple, where the emperors of the former Qing Dynasty had to make a detour to participate in the spring and autumn hunts, has solemn Buddhist statues, mostly made of gold, and the cages, tables, furnaces, and bottles are of unknown origin, mixed with petrified bamboo of various shapes and colors, carved and decorated, which is very beautiful. If our army does not do its best to resist the violent Japanese, I am afraid that the treasures of the Rehe Xinggong Palace will also become exhibits in the Tokyo Museum. 4/18

Japanese Conspiracy to Invade and Disturb Pingjin Reaches

Military and Political Advances Together

Recent Battle Situation Moves to Gubeikou

Special dispatch from Peiping: After the Japanese army occupied the east of the Luo River and the various passes of the Great Wall, although they claimed to have no intention of invading Pingjin, in fact, they take an inch and try to get a mile, and their intentions are huge. Moreover, their conspiracy to invade and disturb Pingjin is divided into two steps, political and military, which is very active. In the political aspect, they use traitors as accomplices and create a special organization in North China. Before Duan Qirui left Tianjin, the Japanese originally intended to use this old man as a puppet. Zeng Yu-jun, Yao Zhen, and others of the Duan family were also eager to try and had close relations with the Japanese. After Duan left Tianjin, the Japanese plan failed, so they changed their method, first resorting to force and then talking about politics. The occupation of Rehe and the east of the Luo River in the past two months is clear evidence of this. Recently, with the military progress, they have also advanced politically. Through traitors such as Li Jichun, they have lured the old warlords in Pingjin and colluded with general frustrated politicians, local tyrants, and evil gentry to carry out activities. As a result, some people who are greedy for wealth and lack firm principles are caught in their trap, and rumors abound, such as the "North China State" movement and the "Protecting the Territory and Protecting the People" movement, which spring up in various forms. Once the brewing is mature, it will erupt. It is said that the authorities are paying close attention and are taking measures to prevent it. In the military aspect, since our army has completely withdrawn to the west of the Luo River, the Japanese army on that side has no active action for the time being, so they have transferred heavy troops to Xifengkou and Gubeikou to conspire to go south along the Pinggu, Sanhe, and Xianghe areas, directly approaching Langfang, cutting off the connection between Pingjin. At the same time, they take a surrounding posture towards Pingjin, causing our Pingjin garrison to withdraw automatically, avoiding fighting near Pingjin, in an attempt to reduce international accusations. For this reason, in recent days, the Japanese army has been using artillery, aircraft, infantry, and cavalry in the Gubeikou area to launch fierce attacks on the left and right wings. Our army has fought bravely. From the 20th to the 23rd, we have been fighting bloodily for three days and nights. The number of deaths and injuries on both sides is over two to three thousand. The battle of Longtangou was particularly fierce, with more than eleven close combats. The positions were contested back and forth five or six times. Our army fell one after another, and their spirit was truly rare. In this battle, two battalion commanders of our Huang Division were killed, one was injured, and the casualties of officers and soldiers reached more than 2,000. The Japanese army's casualties were also comparable. Yesterday (22nd), the battle was fierce all day, and the enemy did not succeed. Our army's front still held the Nantiantianmen position, and the left and right wings were confronting the enemy in the Badaolouzi and Pochengzi areas. Last night, because the enemy had repeatedly failed to attack, they detoured to attack our left wing with a large force. Fortunately, our army detected it and took advantage of the emptiness of the enemy's rear, and urgently dispatched a certain unit at 3:00 a.m. that night, bypassing the enemy's rear from the right wing, and attacked the enemy's brigade headquarters in the Dongguan inside the Gubeikou, killing 500 to 600 enemy soldiers on the spot, capturing more than 30 prisoners, and seizing a lot of military supplies. At about 5:00 a.m. this morning, the enemy learned that their rear had been attacked, and urgently mobilized a large force from the west to return to aid. After our army successfully attacked, they gradually retreated to their original position and held it firmly. The enemy launched a large-scale attack again this afternoon, and fierce fighting is still underway. Our army has stationed more than two divisions in the Gubeikou area, and the military strength is still strong. In the Xifengkou area, the enemy has also been increasing reinforcements in recent days, waiting for an opportunity to attack. There have been artillery battles in the Saho Bridge area yesterday and today. Song Zheyuan has already arrived at the front to command the resistance. (April 23)

Conflict Between Sichuan Armies Liu and Deng

Opening Fire in Jianyang Due to Competition for Power and Profit

Tian Yang and Others Tend to Be Involved in the Vortex

(Chongqing) Communication: Since the ceasefire between the two Lius (劉) in Sichuan Province, the warlords have only known how to expand their own strength and territory, and wantonly exploit the people. A few days ago, Li Jiayu of the 6th New Division and the troops of Tian Songyao of the 29th Army had a conflict in Guihuayuan, Suining, due to a dispute over local tax revenue agencies. Fortunately, the situation did not escalate. After Chairman Chiang Kai-shek sent a telegram and Yang Sen of the 20th Army mediated with armed forces, a storm was quelled. However, one wave was not settled, and another rose. A few days ago, Liu Wenhui of the 24th Army, who had been defeated in battle, felt that the loss of defense was very large, and his income was greatly reduced. The military expenditure was very strained, so he thought of another way out. Because Deng Xihou of the 28th Army had acted in favor of Liu Xiang during the war between the two Lius, causing Liu Wenhui's army to suffer significant losses, Liu proposed conditions to Liu Xihou in order to obtain compensation: (1) Please Deng's army cede the Chengdu Municipal Government to be jointly formed by the armies of Liu and Deng. All monthly income of more than 100,000 yuan will also be divided equally. The mayor will have a head and a deputy, appointed jointly by the armies of Liu and Deng. (2) Chen Shunong, the commander of the 3rd Division of Deng's army, is currently stationed in Hechuan, Tongliang, Wusheng, Bishan, and Dazu counties. He was originally under Liu Wenhui's command, but he defected to Deng's army during the war between the two Lius. Now, the title of commander of the 3rd Division must be revoked and the flag changed. (3) Chen Shunong must return Lezhi, Jianyang, and other counties to Liu's army, otherwise they will meet with soldiers. Deng Xihou refused to recognize all three of the above conditions, which led to a rift with Liu. Liu immediately mobilized the troops of the three divisions, concentrated in Chengdu, and demonstrated to Deng's army. Deng's army also did not yield to each other. Both sides went to extremes, and the guards were strict. In the Lezhi and Jianyang areas, Liu's army had expelled Chen's troops from Deng's army. Yesterday (20th), the two armies formally opened fire in Longquanyi Xiangquanpu and other places, and there is a trend of expansion. Tian Songyao of the 29th Army, Yang Sen of the 20th Army, Luo Zezhou of the 23rd Division, and Li Jiayu and others are also in a state of being involved in the vortex. Currently, the people of Sichuan are actively mediating and calling for peace, but it is difficult to predict whether it will be effective. (April 23)

Water Patrol Team Seizes Stolen Goods Ship

The county water patrol team discovered two suspicious ships in the Xiuye Bridge River today, one from Jiangbei and one from Luhu. Patrol Officer Fei of the team boarded the ships for investigation and found several packages of clothes, many pawn tickets, and gold and silver ornaments, which were obviously of unknown origin. There were two women with Jiangbei accents and a child on board the Jiangbei ship. There was a man on the Luhu ship. After questioning, the woman confessed that the man had taken a car to Shanghai this morning and would return to Songjiang on a late bus, presumably to sell the stolen goods in Shanghai. They were immediately taken back to the team headquarters. When the late bus arrived in Songjiang, they were escorted to the station together with the women to wait for the arrest.

Kunshan

Merchants and People Petition for the Reopening of Pawnshops After the treasurer of Bao Cheng Pawnshop in Dongmen Street absconded with money, the business was suspended and the interior was reorganized. However, the local business was greatly affected, and the poor were even more inconvenienced. Uneven Warmth and Cold, Epidemic Prevails

Due to continuous spring rain, alternating cold and heat, there have been discoveries of epidemic cholera. Wuxi

County Prison Thief Escapes Yu Sanbao, a native of Jiangyin, is 29 years old. In the 19th year of the Republic, he was arrested and sent to the county for gang robbery of silkworm cocoons, and was sentenced to ten years in prison and sent to the county prison to serve his sentence. However, Yu showed a docile attitude after entering prison and was able to work as a mason, so he was often ordered to repair the damaged walls in the prison. Recently, with continuous spring rain, the tiles of the fifth prison room of the county prison were damaged, so prison warden Han Yuwen ordered Yu to repair the roof, and ordered Zhang Yonghuai and Jia Zhengxin, the guards on duty, to keep a close watch. Later, because Yu's feet were chained with heavy shackles, it was inconvenient to go on the roof, so the two guards removed the iron shackles from his left foot. Yu saw that the back of the prison room was the large parade ground of the water police district, and that there was no one in the parade ground. In an instant, he came up with an idea, jumped from the roof, and escaped without a trace. When the two guards discovered it, he was already gone like a crane that has flown away. They immediately reported to prison warden Han, who immediately sent the police team stationed in the county prison to search everywhere, and telegraphed the Public Security Bureau to send police to assist in the arrest. However, Yu had already fled far away and could not be caught. Afterwards, prison warden Han sent the two guards on duty to the county for interrogation and detention, and requested punishment, and submitted Yu's age, height, appearance, and other information to the county government, which was forwarded to the High Court, ordering all subordinates to assist in the arrest.

Peanut Oil Factory Strike

There were as many as 50 peanut oil refining factories in this county at its peak. In recent years, due to the impact of the dumping of Russian oil in China, the business of each factory has declined sharply. About two-thirds of the factories have closed down one after another. In addition, the Ministry of Finance sent personnel to Xishe to collect special business tax on peanut oil. According to the tax collection method, the factory is required to pay a corner of stamp tax for each lift of oil produced every day, and each factory is required to recognize 10 yuan per day. If the factory stops refining, it must report to the collection office in advance, and the collection office will send personnel to seal the furnace and stop collecting taxes. If the refined peanut oil is transported to other ports for sale, the collection office must send personnel to inspect and affix stamps. The factories therefore believe that the loss is very large and cannot bear the burden. Therefore, they went on strike together yesterday, stopped refining, and discussed countermeasures.

Zhenjiang

The Construction Department Bans Native Silkworm Seed The Construction Department has received a telegram from Xia Zhong, the instructor of the Zhenju Lijiang Yi five-county sericulture improvement area, stating that the Zhenju Lijiang Yi five-county sericulture improvement area has now started smoothly. However, after investigation, the local silkworm seeds in each county are still very prevalent. If strict measures are not taken to ban them, it will hinder the improvement work. It is proposed to ask the superior to send a telegram to each county in the improvement area, strictly prohibiting the breeding of local varieties, and those who violate the law will be punished in accordance with Article 21 of the Jiangsu Province Interim Measures for Banning Silkworm Seeds. Is it appropriate to do so? We respectfully request your appraisal and telegraphic instructions for compliance, etc. The Construction Department believes that native silkworm seeds are of poor quality, difficult to breed, and have a significant impact on improving sericulture and increasing the livelihood of farmers. They should be strictly prohibited. It has now instructed each county magistrate to comply immediately.

Huzhou

Three Drowned in Collapsed Pavilion

Residents of Shuanglin Town in Huzhou Prefecture were celebrating the Dongyue Festival at approximately 3 PM on the 22nd of this month when a "Tianqiao Pai" cigarette boat docked at the riverbank outside the Yao Xingchang rice shop and the Wang Jichang fruit shop in the town's North Gate. The boat had a radio playing opera to attract attention, causing men and women watching the festival to crowd into the waterside pavilion to listen. However, the pavilion, which had been in disrepair for years, collapsed under the excessive weight of the crowd, with the roof collapsing at the same time. People on the pavilion all fell into the water. Around sixty or seventy people fell into the water, and fortunately, bystanders managed to rescue them. More than ten people sustained minor injuries, and thirty to forty people sustained serious injuries. The wife of Wang Shunbao, a fruit shop owner, who was over sixty years old, and the wife and daughter of the Xie family boat owner all drowned. The local Public Security Bureau sent police to the scene, detained the cigarette boat and its crew, and the townspeople reported the drowning to the Wuxing branch of the court for inspection of the corpses.

Yu Jia Si, a resident of Yanghu in the Second District of the county, was formerly a battalion commander in a certain military unit and is now retired at home. Local News

Representatives of Cotton Mill Industry Petition in the Capital

Outcome Not Entirely Satisfactory. Rong Zongjing, Nie Lusheng, Guo Shun, Zhang Zemin, representatives of Chinese cotton mills, and Wu Huanru, representative of the Shanghai Municipal Government, arrived in Beijing on the morning of the 25th. According to them, Chinese cotton mills have suffered in recent years from the dumping of Japanese cotton yarn, the bankruptcy of the rural economy, the decline in people's purchasing power, the heavy burden of unified production taxes, and the tightening of bank financing. In Shanghai alone, more than 3.6 million pieces of cotton yarn (each piece containing forty small bales) have accumulated and cannot be sold. In order to maintain the survival of cotton mills and the minimum living standards of workers, a uniform reduction in working hours has been implemented in cotton mills across the country. The Ministry of Industry, the Ministry of Finance, and the Shanghai Municipal Government have sent personnel to investigate the real reasons for the reduction in working hours. After the representatives of each ministry returned to Beijing and reported, the matter was submitted to the Executive Yuan. The Executive Yuan also recognized the seriousness of the matter, believing that if no remedial measures were taken, Chinese cotton mills across the country would be in danger of collapsing entirely, and hundreds of thousands of workers would become unemployed, creating a major panic in China's unemployment problem. Therefore, they summoned the representatives to Beijing to discuss ways to rescue the situation. There are now three requests to the government for relief: (1) The banking sector must provide low-interest loans to manufacturers. Because there are currently more than 3.6 million pieces of cotton yarn in Shanghai, the banking sector has long refused to accept cotton yarn as collateral. In addition to losing interest on the accumulated cotton yarn, there is no way to borrow cash to supplement working capital. This requires the Ministry of Finance and the banking sector to have appropriate measures. (2) A portion of the unified tax revenue must be allocated to rescue manufacturers. Because the unified production tax is levied on both domestic and foreign factory goods, but the tax standards are classified by yarn count. Foreign yarn factories produce more fine yarn, which is very beneficial to foreign merchants. A portion of the tax revenue should be used to rescue Chinese cotton mills. (3) The transportation of cotton and yarn must be expedited, and transportation costs must be reduced. For example, in Zhengzhou and other places, cotton purchased by various factories sometimes takes more than a month to be shipped. The same is true for the shipment of yarn and cloth, which causes significant losses to manufacturers. In the current situation of wind and rain, transportation costs should be reduced even more. A total of sixty-two companies have joined the Chinese Cotton Mill Association, accounting for 77% of the cotton mills in the country. In Shanghai alone, there are approximately 100,000 cotton mill workers. This reduction in working hours will reduce the number of workers by half, which is a significant social problem. Currently, Shanghai, Tongzhou, Wuxi, Zhengzhou, Wuhan, and other places have uniformly implemented the reduction in working hours. Tianjin cabled back to the association yesterday that the current situation is not just a reduction in working hours; the only option is to announce a shutdown. Some cotton mills have already implemented a shutdown, and the remaining cotton mills will also shut down soon. Workers in Shanghai are well aware of the difficulties faced by manufacturers, so no accidents have occurred since the implementation of the reduction in working hours. The scheduled reduction in working hours is for one month. If the government has relief measures, the situation can be restored to its original state next month. The representatives went to the Executive Yuan to meet with Premier Wang, but he was in an administrative meeting and could not meet. In the afternoon, the representatives went to Wang's residence in Sajiawan to discuss the current state of decline in the national cotton industry, its causes, and requested the government to provide appropriate relief in terms of tax rates, transportation, and finance, in order to avoid shutdowns and prevent countless workers from becoming unemployed. Wang agreed to consult with the relevant ministers and make a decision. There was no satisfactory result. It is speculated that these relief measures cannot be decided in a short period of time. The representatives took a train back to Shanghai on the night of the 25th and are scheduled to come to Beijing again.

Cancellation of Loan Contract in the Chen-Li Case of Illegally Pledging the China Merchants Bureau's Four Warehouses

Submitted to the Executive Yuan for Review Based on the Report of the Ministry of Communications

Nanjing, Central News Agency, 25th: After the discovery of the case in which Chen Fumu, the former supervisor of the China Merchants Bureau, and Li Guojie, the former general manager of the Bureau, entered into a loan contract with the China Business Corporation and paid 700,000 taels, the Minister of Communications Zhu Jia Hua repeatedly ordered the board of directors of the Bureau to study methods to cancel the contract and earnestly negotiate with the Corporation to cancel it. The Corporation initially insisted on not agreeing, but Zhu insisted, and the board of directors negotiated earnestly again, and finally agreed to return the funds and terminate the contract, and all related documents were also completely invalidated. It is said that Zhu has submitted the result of the negotiation to cancel the contract to the Executive Yuan for review based on the report of the board of directors.

Philippine Delegation Left for Beijing Last Night

Visited the Central City Area and Factories Yesterday

Will Return to Shanghai and Then to the Philippines after a Two-Day Stay in Beijing

Members of the Japan Study Tour Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, the Philippine Industrial Delegation, consisting of more than thirty people, arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday and immediately checked into the Astor House Hotel on the Garden Bridge. At 9:15 AM yesterday, representatives of various agencies accompanied the delegation to visit the central city area and various factories. Business groups such as the Banking Association and the Shipping Association hosted a banquet for the delegation, which left for Beijing by train last night. The Japan Friendship Study Tour arrived in Shanghai at 8:20 AM yesterday morning. Details are as follows:

Departure for Visit

At 9 AM yesterday, Tang Shixuan, Secretary of the Municipal Government; Li Rongbo, Secretary of the Foreign Affairs Office; Hu Weijian of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Li Zejin of the International Trade Bureau; Tian Heqing of the Social Affairs Bureau; Sun Liping of the Security Bureau; Xue Zhengxin of the Public Works Bureau; Sun Guangyi of the Public Utilities Bureau; and other representatives of various agencies arrived at the Astor House Hotel by car. At 9:15 AM, they accompanied all the members of the delegation, divided into twelve cars, to visit the central city area, Tongji University in Zhabei and Wusong. At 12 PM, they went to the Wing On Cotton Mill, where Guo Shun hosted a lunch. At 1 PM, they departed from the factory to visit Jiaotong University, Xujiahui Observatory, Longhua Scenic Spot, Longhua Cement Company, and Zhanghua Woolen Mill, and finished their visit at around 6 PM, returning to the Astor House Hotel for rest. The Banking Association, the Shipping Association, the Trading Association, and the International Trade Association held a banquet at the Banking Club at 8 PM that night.

Visiting the Cement Factory

Wu Qingtai, the factory director of China Cement Company, and Liu Hongsheng, the representative, greeted and welcomed the delegation. The visiting group was divided into five groups, with five engineers serving as hosts to visit the entire process from rock and mud to cement production and barrel packaging. Then, in the newly completed chemical laboratory of the factory, tea and snacks were served. Wu Qingtai delivered a welcome speech, and the leader of the delegation gave a reply. It was already dusk, so they hurriedly took the Zhanghua Woolen Mill's ferry to Pudong.

Visiting the Zhanghua Factory

When they arrived at Zhoujiadu in Pudong, the lights were already on. However, they still wanted to see China's only woolen factory, so their enthusiasm was not diminished. Cheng Nianpeng, the manager of the factory, and others warmly greeted them and explained the process in detail. They visited every step, from yarn making to weaving, dyeing, and finishing, until the finished camel fleece and serge were produced. The delegation was impressed by the fact that the pure Chinese-made woolen cloth was as exquisite as imported products, and the low price was even more surprising. Ronald specially ordered two sets of white serge, which he will take back to the Philippines for reference and as a souvenir. According to Manager Cheng, the wool raw materials are purely domestic, from Zhejiang and Shandong provinces. Various patterns are being woven, and more complete patterns will be launched in the shortest possible time. After leaving the factory, they took a motorboat back to Shanghai, arriving at the Xinguang Wharf, where the city was already lit up.

More Delegation Members Arriving

The majority of the delegation members and a small number of friendship tour members will arrive in Shanghai tomorrow. There are still more than thirty tourism delegation members remaining in Japan. At 8:20 AM yesterday morning, thirteen men and women tourism delegation members arrived in Shanghai from Japan on the Great Eastern Shipping Company's President Cleveland. After the delegation members landed, they immediately took the cars that were waiting at the customs wharf to the Astor House Hotel for rest. The remaining delegation members staying in Japan will no longer come to Shanghai and plan to return to the Philippines directly from Japan.

Leaving for Beijing Last Night

After the delegation was given a public banquet yesterday by the Banking Association and the Shipping Association, they left for Beijing. The Foreign Affairs Office also negotiated with the Railway Bureau to provide a first-class sleeper car attached to the 11:30 PM express train for the delegation to ride. The Railway Bureau sent two receptionists to take care of them on the train. It is also heard that the delegation plans to stay in Beijing for two days and will return to Shanghai by train on the 27th to take the President Lincoln back to the Philippines on the 28th.

Wenjiang's Remarks

A Central News Agency reporter interviewed Wenjiang, the chairman of the delegation, on the trip yesterday. According to him, he is very grateful for the warm welcome from all walks of life in China. The delegation originally planned to visit Zhao Tiezhang, acting director of the Foreign Affairs Office in Shanghai, and Wang Xiaolai, chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, today (yesterday), but due to the urgency of time, he could not fulfill his wish. After returning to Shanghai from Beijing, he will visit them one by one and plans to take the Lincoln back home on the 29th. Wen also said that after inspecting Japan, he felt that the economic situation in Japan was greatly affected by the world economic panic.
