The Public Concession Has Changed to Collecting Taxes, Water, and Electricity in Silver Dollars

Reply Letter from the Taxpayers' Association to the Federation of Municipal Associations

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession replied to the 20th District Branch of the Federation of Municipal Associations yesterday, stating: Received your letter of April 21 regarding the abolition of the tael and the use of silver dollars. The Public Concession's Board of Directors has replied to the Association's letter of April 10, stating: Received your letter of April 14 regarding the abolition of the tael and the use of silver dollars. Since April 1st, all taxes collected by the Bureau in taels have been converted to silver dollars at a rate of 715. The public utilities of gas and water have also been changed to charge in silver dollars. The method of abolishing taels and changing to silver dollars for telephone and electricity has also been agreed upon. A corresponding reply is hereby given, hoping you will check it. The issues that your association wants to handle have already been resolved. A corresponding reply is hereby given, hoping you will check. Addressed to the 20th District Branch of the Federation of Shanghai Citizens.

Method of Converting Out-of-Town Forward Silver Notes into Silver Coins

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Chongqing Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday to respond to the method of converting forward silver notes into silver coins after the abolition of the tael and the change to silver dollars. The original text reads: Received your telegram and forwarded it to the relevant trade associations of banks and money shops in the city. According to the letter from the Banking Association, after the Ministry's order to implement the abolition of the tael, the Banking Association and the Money Shop Association jointly discussed eight measures, submitted them to the Ministry of Finance for approval, and notified all levels of the court for record. The measures were approved and recorded. Regarding the method for negotiable instruments established before the 15th, Article 7 stipulates: (Forward negotiable instruments that are due before April 15 may be paid in silver dollars at a rate of 715. If the due date is after April 15 but there is no issue date, the original negotiable instrument should be registered with the association before April 15, and silver dollars will be paid at a rate of 715 upon maturity.) Please check and respond. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Two Notices from the Jianghai Customs

Revision of Import Tariff Regulations

Office Closed on May 5th

Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Borel, Commissioner of Customs, jointly issued two notices yesterday regarding the revision of import tariff regulations and the closure of the office on May 5th.

Revising the Tariff

(Omitted above) Now, by order of the government, the provisions of Section 4 of Article 1 of the Import Tariff Regulations should be revised as follows: (Invoices and contracts may be regarded as proof of the price of goods, but they are not necessarily regarded as definitive proof. The interpretation of this point shall be determined by the Customs. In addition to ordering merchants to present invoices and contracts for verification, the Customs may also freely exercise all effective methods, such as inspecting various other documents related to inspection and valuation, investigating detailed sales slips proving both parties, inspecting merchants' books, inspecting goods, and, when necessary, conducting all visits and inviting any private assistance to determine the duty-paid price. The Customs may still inspect the merchants' books at any time for imported goods that have been assessed for duty and released.) You should abide by and handle the matter accordingly. You should inform all merchants, especially to announce this. (Omitted below)

Office Closed

(Omitted above) The Central Executive Committee has stipulated that May 5th is the anniversary of the revolutionary government and should be a holiday. The Customs will be closed on that day and stop working. You should inform all merchants, especially to announce this. (Omitted below)

Residents of Zhabei Petition Against Rent Increase

Residents of Zhenxing Lane on Guangdong Street and the North Sichuan Road area in Zhabei City, approximately one hundred people, were unable to live in peace during the January 28th Incident last year due to Japanese military disturbances and moved elsewhere. However, all the furniture and belongings of these residents were not moved out and remained in the house. At that time, the landlords sealed the houses in the lane. After the end of the war, the residents moved back one after another, and the landlords suddenly demanded that the tenants increase the rent and sign a new lease; otherwise, the seal would not be opened. Some tenants could only temporarily agree because all their furniture had not been moved out. However, these tenants recently opposed the landlord's rent increase, citing that the market in Zhabei City has not yet recovered. The landlord then filed a lawsuit with the local court, which ruled that the tenants should pay the rent in full. The tenants were dissatisfied with the verdict and appealed to the Suzhou High Court. On the 20th of this month, the court decided to conduct a preliminary investigation in Suzhou and decided to first ask the Municipal Land Bureau to investigate the land price situation in the area before making a ruling. The tenants went to the Municipal Government yesterday morning to petition and sent representatives to state the rent situation in the neighboring areas. Secretary-General Yu personally received them and promised to order the Land Bureau to conduct a thorough investigation and report it for review and transfer. The representatives left satisfied.

The Difficult Month of May Is Approaching, Decision to Step Up Security

Prohibition of Associations, Gatherings, and Parades

Commemoration Days Held by Party Headquarters

In view of the fact that the ill-fated month of May is approaching, the municipal Chinese and Concession police agencies have decided to step up security from May 1st to May 30th in order to prevent reactionary elements from disrupting local security under the guise of memorial days. Details are as follows:

Stepped Up Security

There are many commemorative days in May, such as (May 1st) Labor Day, (May 3rd) Jinan Massacre, (May 4th) Student Movement, (May 5th) Premier's Inauguration as Extraordinary President, (May 7th) (May 9th) National Humiliation Day, (May 18th) Martyr Chen Yingshi's Death Anniversary, (May 30th) Nanjing Road Massacre, etc. In order to prevent reactionary elements from taking the opportunity to disrupt local security, Wen Hongen, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and the Public Concession and French Concession police have jointly discussed and decided to step up security from May 1st to May 30th, according to annual practice.

Prohibition of Gatherings

After the Municipal Public Security Bureau decided to step up security in May according to past practice, Director Wen Hongen has ordered the Inspection Department, the Detective Team, and the police stations in each district to comply. All associations, gatherings, parades, etc. are prohibited. The gatherings of legal groups must be submitted to the competent authorities for approval in advance before they can be held, so that the Public Security Bureau can send police to protect them.

Holding Commemorations

The government will simplify the ceremonies for the various revolutionary commemorative days in May during this period of national crisis. The Special Municipal Party Department will only hold commemorations with all sectors of society at the Party Headquarters on Lin Yin Road in Ximen in accordance with the revolutionary commemoration methods stipulated by the central government, such as (May 1st) Labor Day, (May 5th) Premier's Inauguration as Extraordinary President, and (May 18th) Martyr Chen Yingshi's Death Anniversary.

Recent Situation of Overseas Chinese in the Philippines

Talks with Returned Overseas Chinese Fan Changfeng

Enthusiastic Support for Aviation to Save the Country

Japanese Actively Operate in the Philippines

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, since the Philippine Industrial Delegation arrived in Shanghai, various agencies and groups have expressed a warm welcome. A Xin Xin News Agency reporter, in view of the fact that readers want to know about the situation of overseas Chinese in the Philippines, interviewed Fan Changfeng, an overseas Chinese who had recently returned from the Philippines, at the Global Chinese Workers' Union yesterday. With the introduction of Peng Canxian, the executive director of the union, he discussed the recent situation in the Philippines in detail with Fan. The following is a summary of the talks:

Overseas Chinese in the Philippines

There are approximately 90,000 overseas Chinese in the Philippines, mostly from the Southern Fujian counties. Cantonese only account for about three-tenths. Currently, due to the low prices of Philippine native products such as sugar, coconut, coconut fiber, and wood, and the weak purchasing power of the local people, the business of overseas Chinese has also been affected. However, due to the value of gold (one US dollar can be exchanged for two Philippine pesos), one Philippine peso is often worth two and a half Chinese dollars. Therefore, according to a survey by Xiamen Bank, the total amount of money remitted back to China by overseas Chinese in the Philippines each year can still maintain a considerable figure. There are only about 90,000 overseas Chinese in the Philippines, accounting for only one-seventh or one-eighth of the total number of overseas Chinese. However, they are the most enthusiastic in donating to national affairs. For example, during the January 28th Shanghai War, when the 19th Route Army resisted the Japanese in Shanghai, they remitted more than 800,000 dollars in one month, accounting for one-sixth of all overseas Chinese donations, which shows their enthusiasm.

Southern Advance and Northern Advance

The Japanese aggression abroad is divided into the Southern Advance and the Northern Advance. The Northern Advance refers to the operation of Manchuria in China, while the Southern Advance refers to the development of the Nanyang Islands. However, the commercial rights of the Nanyang Islands are still in the hands of overseas Chinese. Therefore, the Japanese deliberately use the power of the state to attack the overseas Chinese in an organized and planned manner. Because of the losses suffered from the boycott by overseas Chinese in the past, they decided to directly trade with the natives after the Jinan Massacre. They actively prepared for this on weekdays. Therefore, since the September 18th Incident occurred the year before last, after the overseas Chinese in the Philippines implemented a boycott of Japanese goods, the number of Japanese shops has increased instead. For example, in the city of Cagayan, there was only one Japanese shop before the September 18th Incident, but now there are eight. In Iligan, there were only four or five, but now there are more than twenty. At the same time, the overseas Chinese are affected by the depression on the one hand, and the Japanese economic aggression on the other hand. The closure of shops is heard every day. The situation of one prosperity and one decline is very dangerous. It is hoped that the overseas Chinese affairs authorities of our country will pay attention and find ways to remedy the situation; otherwise, the day of collapse is not far away.

Japanese Ambition

The Philippine Islands are an important island in the Pacific Ocean. The city of Davao at the southernmost tip of the Philippines is just a small place that has just been developed, but the number of Japanese residents has reached 20,000. They buy land in the name of natives and ostensibly engage in agriculture. They build their own docks and warehouses, and ships often sail directly from Japan to the port. The city has a magnificent consulate and a Japanese association, as well as a Japanese-style garden church. They are actively operating and spare no effort. Now, the educated Filipinos regard Davao City as a second Manchuria because of its military deployment, and its ambition is gradually being exposed. This year, the Philippine Congress passed a bill to redeem the land there from the Japanese government at a price set by the Philippine government, and negotiations are currently underway.

Reasons for Anti-Chinese Sentiment

The Chinese arrived in the Philippines hundreds of years before the Spanish ruled the Philippines. According to historical records, they had contact with the Filipinos as early as the 13th century. Therefore, the relationship between the Chinese and the Filipinos has always been friendly.

Page 8

Moreover, more than 70% of Filipinos have Chinese blood. In recent years, due to the popularity of education and the gradual opening of knowledge among Filipinos, and the frequent internal turmoil in our country and the decline in international status, the local natives have a contemptuous attitude towards overseas Chinese. Since the loss of Dong Province due to non-resistance in the September 18th Incident, the Filipinos have shown more contempt for the overseas Chinese. They often scold the overseas Chinese as Manchurian slaves when they meet on the road. Moreover, the Japanese provoke hostility between the Chinese and the Filipinos, creating an anti-Chinese psychology among the Filipinos in order to achieve their conspiracy to seize the status of the overseas Chinese. Therefore, overseas Chinese in the Philippines often face unequal treatment. For example, Chinese immigrants are often harassed by customs officials and detained in a room called a "water prison." It is said that Mr. Huang Shaoxiong also suffered this hardship when he went to the Philippines last year. Overseas Chinese are almost always rejected by the natives, not only in the Philippines. This is indeed the biggest obstacle to our overseas development.

Saving the Country Through Aviation

Recently, the idea of saving the country through aviation has been widely promoted, and overseas Chinese are particularly enthusiastic in supporting it. Last winter, General Weng Zhaoyuan, representing the Chinese Aviation Construction Association, went to the Philippines to carry out association affairs. In less than two months in the Philippines, more than twenty branch associations were established, and approximately 20,000 people joined as members. The membership fee revenue was approximately 200,000 Chinese dollars. Later, the association affairs were suspended due to the merger of the general association. Otherwise, the results would have been even more impressive.

Discussing Improving Rural Life

Exhibition of Homemade Cloth Held at the Same Time

Ministry of Industry Orders All Fishing Areas to Reorganize National Fishing Vessels

Re-numbering Free in Jiangzhe Area

According to the National Society, the Ministry of Industry believes that my country's fishing industry is declining, and coastal aquatic products are being plundered by strong neighbors. Therefore, it intends to rectify national fishing vessels, re-number them, and improve them. Therefore, it has specially instructed the fishery administrations of Jiangzhe, Jilu, Minyue and other regions to stipulate three measures: (1) The Jiangzhe area will re-number fishing boat license plates from July 1 this year. All license fees will no longer be collected because the Jiangzhe Fishery Improvement Association has already collected construction fees. (2) The fishery bureaus of Jilu and Minyue will also set to start numbering fishing boat license plates from July 1 this year. Each plate will be priced at 30 cents of ocean currency, divided into three types, A, B, and C, for identification. (3) All license plate styles will be stipulated by the Ministry, and the regional bureaus will be ordered to manufacture and issue them themselves to save procedures. The above three measures have been ordered to be complied with.

Pencil Lead Mine Discovered in Shaanxi Province; International Trade Bureau Chemical Test Report

Carbon Content Reaches 94 Percent, Better Than Japanese Goods, Comparable to American Goods Shaanxi Province is located in the northwest with vast regions and rich natural resources. There are countless abandoned resources due to a lack of development. Recently, the Shaanxi Provincial Department of Construction has been actively engaged in surveying and mapping, and has recently discovered a graphite mine (i.e., pencil lead mine) near the Qinling Mountains in the province. The abundance of its mineral resources is surprising to the outside world. However, the authorities in the province are unaware of the price of pencil lead and are not familiar with the sales methods. Therefore, they specially dispatched Zhao Guobin, a technician from the department, to Shanghai to contact the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry to discuss everything. After the bureau conducted a chemical test, it was deemed that the mineral quality was excellent and has been widely promoted. The letter from the Shaanxi Construction Department and the chemical test report of the International Trade Bureau are recorded below:

Letter from Shaanxi Construction Department

The original letter from the Shaanxi Provincial Department of Construction to the International Trade Bureau states: "Respectfully, this department has recently initiated the graphite mining industry in Shaanxi Province and intends to find a large sales market in other areas. The quality of this mineral has been repeatedly appraised by experts, who believe it is most suitable for manufacturing pencils and carbon rods for electrical purposes. However, information is needed regarding the market price of graphite, whether it should be delivered in Shaanxi or Shanghai, the value of each 100-jin load, and how sales should be conducted before operations can be handled. Your esteemed bureau has comprehensive knowledge of international trade and a thorough understanding of Chinese and foreign commercial information. Therefore, this department has dispatched technician Zhao Guobin to contact you and bring a package of mineral samples for your inspection. We kindly request your guidance and will welcome your assistance in introducing sales merchants. Responding letter from the International Trade Bureau is highly appreciated. This letter is respectfully addressed to the International Trade Bureau."

Chemical Test Report

According to the International Trade Bureau's chemical test of the sample of pencil lead ore brought to Shanghai, it is believed that its carbon content is comparable to that of American products. It is found that pencil lead ore is a recent discovery in China. In the past, the Chinese market needed this raw material, which was supplied by the United States and Japan. The products from the United States are of excellent quality, with a carbon content of up to 96 percent, and the price is up to 400 yuan per ton. The products from Japan are not as good, with a carbon content of only 70 percent, and the price is only between 130 yuan and 160 yuan per ton. However, when used to manufacture dry batteries, they are far inferior to American goods, often only emitting light for 40 hours before turning red and going out. Now, the carbon content of our country's products is as high as 94 percent, which is almost the same as American goods. Therefore, it is a good opportunity for our country to resist the import of Japanese pencil lead.

Letter of Introduction to Hong Kong

After the bureau determined the quality to be excellent through chemical testing and clarified the market price, it sent a letter to the Shaanxi Construction Department and yesterday sent a letter to the Hong Kong Tianhua Pencil Factory to introduce it. The factory is owned by Chinese merchants and is the only pencil factory among Chinese merchants, so it specially informed them that they can use domestic products as much as possible in the future. As for other merchants who want to use this raw material, they can also inquire about the truth from the International Trade Bureau. It is said that this pencil contains a lot of [blank], but the Shaanxi Provincial Government is not willing to announce it. As for the transportation method in the future, it will first be transported from the place of production to [blank] and then transported along the Longhai Railway to Haizhou, and then transshipped to Shanghai.

Universal Postal Union to Be Held Next Year

Preparatory Meeting to Be Held First in June According to the Central News Agency, regarding the convening of the Universal Postal Union Congress, yesterday's report stated that the current session will be held in Argentina, and my country will submit issues such as Japan instigating rebels to seize postal rights in the Northeast to the Congress for discussion. Yesterday, a Central News Agency reporter inquired about this matter from the highest-ranking official of the Directorate General of Posts. According to the talk, the Universal Postal Union is dedicated to handling international postal affairs, and political and diplomatic issues are beyond the jurisdiction of this conference. The rumor that my country will submit the issue of the Japanese instigating rebels to seize postal rights and request sanctions is not clear about the organization of the Postal Union. The current Congress is planned to be held in Cairo, Egypt, in early February next year. According to past practice, a preparatory meeting must be held before the convening of the Congress to review the Congress's proposals. The preparatory meeting will be held in Paris in mid-June. As for our country's representatives, they have not yet been appointed.

Ministry of Industry Informs Municipal Government to Re-Instruct Measurement and Correction Review Free of Charge

Difficulty in Changing Inspection Fee Collection Regulations The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously submitted a letter from the Weights and Measures Association, requesting the Ministry of Industry to reduce inspection fees and waive the re-inspection fee after correction, stating that the inspection fee collection regulations issued by the Ministry of Industry stipulated that the collection fee was twice or several times higher than the various inspection fees previously collected in this city. Also, according to the usual practice, repeatedly inspected instruments, whether qualified or not, must be paid for. If there are slight differences, when they are corrected and sent for inspection, they must still be paid for item by item, which the industry cannot afford. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Industry requesting to reduce the weights and measures inspection fee collection fee and approve free re-inspection to relieve the industry's difficulties. Yesterday, the Municipal Government received a consultation from the Ministry of Industry stating (the above is omitted): "The regulations for the collection of weights and measures inspection fees have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for filing, and the Ministry of Industry has announced its implementation. It is difficult to change. However, for unqualified instruments, re-inspection after correction should not be charged separately in order to relieve business difficulties and reduce costs. In addition to the approval, you are hereby consulted to investigate and re-instruct the Social Affairs Bureau to comply with the above."

Guohua Silk Factory Labor Unrest Alleviated

Resumed Work Under the Advice of the Social Affairs Bureau The Guohua Silk Weaving Factory in Dongbaziqiao, Henan Road, Zhabei, with more than 170 workers, recently demanded that the factory restore the reduced wages, opposed the factory's independent change of the workers' national salvation donation to aviation national salvation, and opposed the unreasonable voluntary letter (the content of which required workers to be dismissed six months after filling it out). The opposition of all the workers caused a full-scale strike the day before yesterday and filed a petition with the Social Affairs Bureau. At ten o'clock yesterday morning, in order to avoid the expansion of the situation, the Social Affairs Bureau specially sent mediator Tan Peiyan to investigate. They immediately ordered the resumption of work and requested that the parties submit all sections and quietly await mediation. All the factory workers resumed work uniformly from yesterday afternoon.

Seafarers' Union Investigates the Situation of Workers on Japanese Vessels

Since the 918 Incident two years ago, the Changjiang class Luoyang, Fengyang, Nanyang, Xiangyang, Dazhen, Daji, Ruiyang, Yueyang, Dafu, Dali and other vessels under the jurisdiction of Nisshin Company have suffered a sharp decline in business due to the fact that the majority of Chinese people do not take Japanese ships and load goods. Except for the four vessels Luoyang, Xiangyang, Fengyang and Nanyang, which are still operating, the four vessels Yueyang, Ruiyang, Dazhen and Daji have long been suspended. More than 400 workers on the four vessels have now no work to do. The two ships Da, Fu and Dali were recently dismantled by the company, and all the machinery and equipment have been transported back to the country one after another. The 175 Chinese workers in various departments of the two ships were also unconditionally dismissed. The Seafarers' Union believes that the livelihood of hundreds of Chinese workers is precarious after this blow, and has now sent people to investigate the situation of workers on the company's suspended ships and submit it to the Central Government for assistance.

Passerby in Western Suit Helps Police Arrest a Thief

A stray bullet wounds a student

The Victim Recounts the Incident

At 7:40 the night before last, five bandits suddenly came to the house of Sun Maojian at No. 294 North Henan Road. Three bandits climbed upstairs and used pistols to threaten them to remain silent. Just as they were about to start searching, Sun's mother took advantage of the gap to slip out of the back door and reported to the nearby Constable No. 457 and Chinese Constable No. 2163. The constables arrived and encircled the area, sounding the siren loudly. The bandits became anxious and rushed out the door and fled in different directions. The two constables saw that the bandits were holding pistols and feared being ambushed, so they opened fire. As a result, a passerby in a western suit helped capture a thief named Xu Canxiong. Two gold watches worth 100 yuan were found on his person and taken to the Hongkou Police Station. Yesterday morning, the police station sent the suspect to the Third Criminal Division of the Shanghai First Special District Local Court. Judge Wu Zehan took his seat to interrogate the suspect. The police station's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the case, saying that when the Chinese and Indian constables opened fire, a stray bullet injured a student named Wang. After receiving treatment at Renji Hospital, the hospital notified the police station by telephone. The student is still under treatment and cannot appear in court to testify, so he requested a postponement. The original stolen gold watches were then presented for inspection. Then, according to the victim Sun Maojian's statement in the case, at that time, three bandits climbed upstairs. The defendant slapped me in the ear, and another bandit in black clothes pointed a gun at my neck, threatening me to remain silent and making me lie on the table. The gold watches presented in the case are indeed the stolen goods. Also, according to the witness Jiang Xiaolong, he was a newspaper vendor. At that time, he saw the defendant running away, and someone behind him shouted "Thief!" and chased after him. I also chased after him and then saw a person in a western suit capture him. When asked, the defendant confessed. After Judge Wu verified the confession, he ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody for further interrogation at a later date.

Dispute Over Jointly Stored Valuables in Safe Deposit Box

Lian Rong Exploits a Vulnerable Person

Devouring All the Jewelry

Rong Li Xiaojun, a young woman residing at 42 Rue Massenet, in her blossoming years, had, around 1929, stored valuable jewelry and her husband Rong Wenhao's valuables in safe deposit box number 311 at Jin Cheng Bank. Lian Rong, her husband's sister, also placed her jewelry in the same safe deposit box. Everything was stored under Rong Wenhao's name. Lian Rong held the key to the box, while Rong Li Xiaojun possessed the impression seal for withdrawals. In February of last year, Rong Wenhao suddenly disappeared. Lian Rong seized the opportunity to trick her sister-in-law into handing over the safe deposit box seal. She went to the bank alone and removed all the items from the box, then stored them under a different name. Last summer, Rong Li Xiaojun, needing jewelry, invited her aunt to retrieve it. Upon opening the box, they found it completely empty, with only four and a half sheets of old newspaper remaining. Initially, Lian Rong refused to admit that the items were in her possession. Later, her son explained the situation to Rong Li Xiaojun, leading to negotiations. Lian Rong repeatedly claimed that because Shanghai was about to become unstable, she had taken the items out and intended to take them to Hong Kong. She also argued that all the stored items were her brother's property, and she was entitled to manage them. However, Rong Li Xiaojun insisted that the jewelry was her private property and could not be devoured by Lian Rong. The two women argued back and forth, unable to reach a resolution. Rong Li Xiaojun then filed a civil lawsuit against Lian Rong, and although the court ordered the disputed

jewelry to be seized, enforcement proved difficult, and the items have yet to be recovered. Now, Rong Li Xiaojun has filed a criminal suit against Lian Rong, seeking to have her prosecuted for theft. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui of the First Special District Court held a hearing. The defendant, Lian Rong, residing at No. 14, Jue Yuan, at the intersection of Rue A. Cohen and Rue Ha Tong, had been summoned by the court police, but she failed to appear. The plaintiff, Rong Li Xiaojun, then presented her account of how she and the defendant jointly stored the jewelry, how the defendant tricked her into handing over the safe deposit box key, and how all the stored items were taken by the defendant and refused to be returned. Judge Liu stated that the plaintiff had not provided a detailed list of the items taken by the defendant. Therefore, he ordered the plaintiff to provide a list and instructed the court to summon the defendant to appear for a hearing on May 8th in the afternoon.

Taxpayers' Association Requests the Shanghai Municipal Council to Correct the Assessed Rental Values of Properties

To Prevent Disputes Arising from Water Charges. The Chinese Ratepayers’ Association of the Shanghai International Settlement sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "To the Director-General: Having examined the experimental measures for water charges based on meter readings, effective from April 1st, this Association believes that this is a practical policy aimed at seeking actual costs. However, the rental values upon which the charges are based do not comply with the regulations of the agreement dated December 24, 1931. The rental values assessed by your Council are often higher than the actual values, and in many cases, the water charges included in the rental fees are not deducted. In order to avoid unnecessary disputes in the future, we request that your Council make corrections accordingly." This letter was addressed to the Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement.

Sheng Yuchang Indictment for Seduction and Abandonment Case

Two Witnesses Appeared in Court Yesterday

The Judge Still Hopes for Reconciliation Between the Man and Woman

Sheng Yuchang, currently residing at 1 Avenue Petain in the French Concession, grandson of the former Qing official Sheng Xingxun, was previously sued in the Second Special District Court by Yan Minghan, Yan Qu Shi, and their daughter Yan Shuangqin, residents of Route de Canton, who hired lawyers Dong Kang and Zhang Zhirang to represent them. They filed a criminal complaint alleging that Sheng Yuchang had seduced and abandoned Shuangqin after a prolonged relationship. On the afternoon of January 23rd of this year, the case was heard by presiding Judge Wang Gangxu of the Criminal Court, who ordered Sheng to provide a guarantor who would ensure his appearance whenever summoned, and instructed both parties to attempt reconciliation outside of court before resuming proceedings. This was reported previously. The case remains unresolved due to the ongoing dispute between the parties. Yesterday afternoon, the trial resumed. The plaintiffs, Yan Minghan and his wife, did not attend, but Yan Shuangqin arrived at court with her lawyers, Dong and Zhang. The defendant also arrived with his lawyer, Qiu Fenling. At 3:00 PM, Judge Wang opened the Second Criminal Court and summoned the parties and their lawyers to the courtroom. He first questioned them about their ages and origins. The plaintiff, Yan Shuangqin, stated that she was 26 years old, born on the sixth day of the eleventh month of the first year of Xuantong (1909), and a native of Shanghai. The defendant, Sheng Yuchang, stated that he was 37 years old, from Wujin, Jiangsu, and a businessman. The judge asked Yan Shuangqin if she had attempted reconciliation since the last hearing. She replied that the defendant had not sent anyone to discuss it. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer, Zhang, stated that further evidence of abandonment had emerged. He explained that because the defendant had failed to pay the

Police Rates

and utilities for two months, the water and electricity to Yan Shuangqin's residence had been cut off. As water and electricity are necessities, the plaintiff informed her lawyer, who sent a letter to the defendant requesting payment. However, the fees remain unpaid. The lawyer presented a copy of the letter as evidence. The judge then asked Yan Shuangqin when the defendant had stopped visiting her. She replied that he had not been there since November of last year. The judge asked her if she still wished to live with the defendant. She replied that she did not. He then asked when their relationship began. She replied between August and September of 1927. The plaintiff's lawyer, Zhang, stated that Yan Shuangqin had been betrothed to Wu Xiusheng since childhood. However, upon learning of her relationship with the defendant, Wu had sent a letter requesting the dissolution of the engagement. The original letter was presented as evidence. Gu Jue knew of the relationship between the two, and both Wu and Gu had been summoned to testify and could be called. The judge ordered the two witnesses to leave the courtroom. He then summoned Wu Xiusheng to testify, first administering an oath. Wu stated that he was 26 years old, from Shanghai, residing at 521 Route de Krug, and currently a fourth-year law student at Soochow University. He stated that he did not know Sheng Yuchang, but he had known Yan Shuangqin

Since Childhood Through an Engagement

The judge gave Wu the letter to read, and Wu confirmed that he had written it in February of 1930, upon hearing rumors of her cohabitation with Sheng. He stated that he had sent the letter requesting the dissolution of the engagement. The judge then asked the defendant, Sheng Yuchang, if he knew that Yan Shuangqin had been previously engaged to Wu. He replied that he had not known initially, but later Shuangqin had told him that she had an engagement with Yu Yuanzhuang. He was unable to recall when she had told him this. The court then called witness Gu Jue (female), administering an oath. Gu stated that she was 21 years old, from Shanghai, and worked in education. She stated that Yan Shuangqin was a friend. (The Judge asked) Do you know of the relationship between Yan Shuangqin and Sheng Yuchang? (Answer) I know a little bit about it. Around August or September of 1927, around 2 PM, I went to the Yan's house, and at 5 PM, Mr. Sheng arrived in a car to pick up Shuangqin to go out. Shuangqin invited me to go with them. We went to the Cangzhou Hotel. Later, I saw that they were very intimate, and I felt embarrassed to leave first. I do not know when they returned home. Several days later, I went to the Yan's house again, and Shuangqin told me that after we had been out,

Mr. Sheng had her

Stay overnight. (Question) Where did you depart from in the car that day? (Answer) We departed from the Yan's house on Route de Canton. The judge asked Sheng Yuchang, "Do you know the witness Gu Jue?" Sheng replied, "I do not know her. I have never met her." Sheng then said to Gu, "I do not know you." Gu replied, "I know you." The judge then asked Yan Shuangqin, "When you were living with Sheng, were you his wife or his concubine?" She answered, "He promised to marry me." (Question) Did you know if he had a wife? (Answer) He was in the process of divorcing his wife. He promised me that after he divorced, he would marry me. (Question) Was there a marriage? (Answer) He always delayed it, and we never married. (Question) Where did you live together, and where did the money for your daily expenses come from? (Answer) In May 1930, we lived together in the Lafayette Apartments, and he gave me money. (Question) What was the nature of your cohabitation? (Answer) He told me to wait for him.... (Question) Were you marrying him as a concubine? (Answer) No. (Question) Was it cohabitation? She did not answer. The judge then asked Sheng Yuchang, "When did you meet and begin your relationship?" Sheng answered, "I met and began my relationship in May 1930. I met her on Route de Canton. At first, we were strangers, but later,

We often went to see movies

and gradually became familiar." (Question) Did you agree to take her as a concubine? (Answer) No. She asked me herself and wanted to marry me as a concubine. However, because I already had two wives at home, I did not agree. (Question) Do you know how old she is this year? (Answer) I know that she is 26 years old this year. (Question) How were her living expenses paid when you lived together? (Answer) There was no specific living expense. She asked me for money, and I gave her some. The plaintiff's lawyer just said that I did not pay the police rates, but I have never paid that fee. (He also said) Her father is a Taoist priest. We first met during a Buddhist ceremony in a temple. (Question) After this case occurred, Shuangqin asked you for three thousand yuan. What was that about? (Answer) After her brother-in-law was kidnapped, I went to see her at the Lafayette Apartments. She was managing her brother-in-law's move, etc. Later, without my agreement, she moved into my house on Guofu Min Road. I tried to stop her, but she said that she had nowhere to go and wanted to live there, and she asked me to give her some money. I said that even if I didn't go, it wouldn't matter. I didn't agree, and then she asked me for three thousand yuan. After questioning to this point, the judge said to Sheng, "You have known each other for several years. It is always best to reconcile." Sheng replied, "I agree to reconcile and am very grateful for the court's good intentions. However, Shuangqin's side also needs to make some concessions." The judge then said to the lawyers of both parties, "It is still best for the lawyers of both parties to reconcile outside the court." Both responded in agreement. The judge then announced that the case would be adjourned for three weeks and ordered the parties to reconcile outside of court. If reconciliation is not possible, then a date will be set for further questioning. The court then adjourned.

The Council, at its executive committee meeting yesterday afternoon around 5 o'clock, deemed them satisfactory. It was also decided to notify all businesses in the French Concession today that all business should be resumed, and a meeting of all businesses in the French Concession will be convened at 3:00 PM this afternoon to report on the results of the mediation and to express gratitude to the French authorities for their sincerity in peacefully resolving the situation and for their consideration of the merchants' difficulties.

Doctors of Traditional Chinese Medicine Oppose Taxation of Prescriptions

The Shanghai Branch of Traditional Chinese Medicine is implementing a policy of collecting fees for medicines, equivalent to one cent per prescription. It is said that the implementation has been agreed upon. However, this matter resembles the collection of a surtax. Since the branch is not an administrative agency, it should not exercise this privilege. Various TCM organizations here believe it is illegal and have risen in opposition. They convened a joint meeting of various medical groups the day before yesterday, with over sixty executive and supervisory committee members attending. A presidium was elected, and a unanimous resolution was passed to express opposition. However, the entire body supported the idea of raising funds to maintain the medical association.

Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange Convenes Shareholders' Meeting Regarding Merger

The Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange and the securities department of the Chinese Merchant Commodities Exchange were ordered to merge last year. Due to issues regarding proportions (the commodities and securities department demanded a 50/50 split in trading volume, while the securities exchange only agreed to a 70/30 split), a suitable method has not been found, and the merger has not been implemented. Yesterday, the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange sent a letter to its shareholders to discuss this matter at a meeting this Sunday (the 30th) afternoon. The letter stated: "To the Director-General: In accordance with Article 55 of the Exchange Law and Article 16 of the Exchange's articles of association, a special shareholders' meeting will be held at the Exchange at 2:00 PM on Sunday, April 30, 1933, to discuss the merger and related matters, as well as to report on the lawsuit filed by Wei Zhu et al. In addition to publishing a public notice, a letter has been sent accordingly. Enclosed are a copy of the meeting agenda, an admission ticket, four voting slips (for and against), and a proxy form. Please verify receipt. As this matter is important, we urge you to attend the meeting in person with your ticket."

Pudong Bank Establishes Branch and Warehouse

Another Branch Established in Zhoupu Zhoupu is located in the center of Pudong, at the crossroads of Nanhui, Chuansha, Xinchang, Datuan, and Fengxian Xiasha. Railways and roadways provide convenient transportation. It holds the pivotal point of commerce and is indeed an important town in Pudong. However, the lack of financial institutions is regrettable. The Pudong Commercial Savings Bank of this city aims to develop the Pudong market, revitalize Pudong commerce, adjust finances, and promote savings. In addition to establishing a branch in Laiyidu in Pudong, it now plans to establish a Zhoupu branch and warehouse. The location has been selected on West Market Street, and the interior decoration is complete. The opening ceremony is scheduled for the 30th of this month. It is also heard that during the opening period, the savings department will provide exquisite leather wallets, valuable silk fans, and gold-label champagne tickets as gifts.

Latest News from the Vocational Guidance Institute

The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute held its 14th discussion meeting at 9:00 AM the day before yesterday, with over 130 attendees. The meeting focused on discussing employment issues, and Mr. Shi Jiuyun, Mr. Pan Yangyao, and Mr. Yang Chonggao attended to provide guidance, which was of great interest. Due to the large number of questions raised, the remaining questions will be discussed at the next meeting. Recently, the institute was commissioned by a bank in this city to recruit clerical staff. Applicants must be over 14 years old and under 18 years old, in good health, have the equivalent of an upper primary school education, be of good character, be agile, be able to endure hardship, and have a reliable business guarantee. Those willing to apply can go to the institute to register. Approximately eight people will be selected for the initial test, followed by a second test. Only those who pass the second test will be hired by the bank. They must first undergo a one-month trial period, during which they will be provided with accommodation and a monthly meal allowance of ten yuan. After three years of service, these clerical staff can be promoted to trainees and can attend evening school to continue their education. In order to facilitate higher education for young people across the country, the institute is surveying the content, curriculum, and current admission situation of well-known universities, specialized schools, secondary schools, vocational schools, and normal schools in various regions to compile a "Higher Education Guide." This guide will facilitate young people's selection of schools and include essays by education experts to guide prospective students. Currently, the institute is surveying various parties and collecting materials. It is expected to be published around early June, priced at twenty cents. Young people across the country who wish to subscribe can pre-order from the institute on Hualong Road.

Lou Zhenfan, an officer of the First Sub-Bureau of the Minhang Public Security Bureau in the county, was previously stationed at the Fourth Sub-Bureau in Sanlintang. While there, he led a police raid on a gambling den, injuring civilians, which caused public outrage. County Magistrate Tang dispatched an inspector general to investigate, and the facts were confirmed. Yesterday, County Magistrate Tang issued an order to dismiss Lou from his post and appointed Yang Xi to succeed him. In addition, Zheng Yisheng, the captain of the county government's detective team, was found to have performed his duties improperly and was dismissed from his post by County Magistrate Tang yesterday. A replacement will be appointed separately.

Verdict in the Marking Club Dispute Murder Case

Jiang Boxian, a seller of used clothing residing at No. 12 Xingju Lane, East End of Qinglong Bridge, Nanshi, organized a rotating credit association. Zhou Ronggui, the owner of Zhou Wansheng Noodle Shop, and his sister-in-law each registered one share. His sister-in-law received the funds and remarried elsewhere. Zhou then won the association at the end of the lunar year. Jiang, having learned from the previous case, demanded a guarantor. Zhou then brought gangsters to threaten him with guns. Jiang's wife, Jiang Wu Shi, went outside to report to police officer Liu Lindong that there was a robbery. Liu entered the house without asking any questions and immediately opened fire, shooting and killing Zhou Ronggui at point-blank range. After investigation by the local court, a public prosecution was initiated. After repeated trials and debates in the Criminal Court, Judge Qian opened court yesterday afternoon to announce the verdict. Liu Lindong was sentenced to three years and six months imprisonment for homicide. Jiang Wu Shi was sentenced to four months imprisonment for false accusation. Jiang Boxian was found not guilty.

Trial Record of the Axe Murder of Cao Anan

Around 7:00 PM on May 20th last year (15th day of the fourth lunar month), the incident of Cao Anan being killed with an axe occurred at the Qichangzhan Siming Guild Hall in Pudong. The local bailiff reported it to the court, which dispatched personnel to examine the body, prepare the coffin, and await the arrest and prosecution of the murderer. It has now been learned that this case was a revenge killing. The deceased, Cao Anan, and Zhou Axiang, Zhou Jinshan, Wang Qiugen, etc. were all carpenters and had known each other for a long time. Recently, because Cao Anan did not engage in honest work, he repeatedly borrowed money from Zhou Axiang and others and extorted them on various pretexts. Zhou and others, unable to bear the burden, decided to murder Cao to eliminate future troubles. Zhou Axiang initiated and implemented the plan. After the deceased's mother, Zhou Mei, learned of the details, she filed lawsuits with the local court and public security bureau, seeking a thorough investigation. The bureau ordered the police to arrest Wang Qiugen, and after questioning him, they transferred the suspect to the court for trial. The prosecutor interrogated him, and the facts were confirmed. The suspect confessed in court. Zhou Axiang and Zhou Jinshan are still at large and will be dealt with separately upon their capture. Wang Qiugen was prosecuted by the criminal court under Article 284, Paragraph 1, Item 1 of the Criminal Code and Article 253, Paragraph 1, Item 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law, requesting a public trial. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Judge Luo Renji specially opened the First Tribunal for trial, and the court-appointed attorney, Sha Xunyi, attended the court to defend the defendant. After the judge took his seat, he ordered the incarcerated Wang Qiugen to be brought before the court. Wang testified that he was 26 years old, from Nanhui, residing at the house of Shen Xukui in Shenjia Nong, Pudong, for four or five years, and had been a carpenter. (Question) Who is in your family? (Answer) I have a mother and a 23-year-old younger brother, who is a coppersmith. (Question) What was the occupation of the deceased, Cao Anan? (Answer) He was also a carpenter. (Question) On what day, at what place, and with whom did you kill Cao Anan? (Answer) Around 7:00 PM on the 15th day of the fourth lunar month last year, Zhou Axiang and I killed him with an axe in the Siming Guild Hall area in Pudong. Zhou Axiang struck first, and then Axiang forced me to strike, so I struck once on the ground. (Question) You confessed clearly in the prosecutor's office that you struck him on the head. (Answer) I really struck him on the ground. (Question) Who initiated the plan? (Answer) Zhou Axiang initiated the plan. At that time, Zhou Axiang asked me to go out with him. (Question) Did the deceased have any grudges against you? (Answer) No. Moreover, Anan and I were cousins. (Question) You confessed to the prosecutor that the deceased was a hooligan who often borrowed money from you and extorted you. (Answer) The deceased did have a difficult relationship with Zhou Axiang. (Question) How did you go there at that time? (Answer) Zhou Axiang asked me to go out for a stroll with him. When we arrived at the Siming Guild Hall area, Zhou Axiang took out an axe and tried to chop Anan. I stepped forward to stop him, but Axiang kicked me down. Zhou then chopped Cao Anan down from behind, and then Zhou Jinshan pressed Anan down. Axiang forced me to chop, but Anan was already dead. (Question) Are Zhou Axiang and Zhou Jinshan brothers? (Answer) Yes. (Question) Did Shen Xukui know about it? (Answer) He didn't know. After the judge recorded the testimony, he said to the lawyer Sha Xunyi, "The plaintiff has not arrived today. We will set another date for a continued trial." The judge then adjourned the court.

Although the Young Woman Comes from a Poor Background, Her Good Looks Have Brought Her Disaster

Qian Abing Can Be Described as a Wolf in Human Clothing

After Defiling Her, He Plotted to Sell Her

Wang Yaoshi, a woman from Jiangbei, is currently 18 years old and works as a factory girl at the Shanghai Yong'an Third Cotton Mill, residing on Rue Mequin. Although she comes from a poor background, she is not unattractive. Qian Abing, 23 years old, a fellow villager, seeing that she is young and easily deceived, used seduction tactics and sweet words. On the afternoon of the 21st of this month, around 6:00 PM, he waited at the factory gate. When she finished work, he coaxed her in every way, and she was lured to the home of his friend, Xu Ruyou, at No. 56 Da Tong Road in the New Concession, where she was imprisoned and not allowed to leave. The next day, he forcibly raped Wang Yaoshi and plotted to secretly transport her to Fujian to sell for profit. Unexpectedly, his plan was uncovered by Chinese detectives Fang Qingyun and Bao Tan Chen Jinsheng of the Council Police. The detectives secretly went to No. 56 Da Tong Road the day before yesterday, arrested Qian and Xu Ruyou, rescued Wang Yaoshi, and took them back to the police station separately. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stated the case, saying that the police are now prosecuting Qian Abing for the crime of disrupting the family under Article 257, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code, and Xu Ruyou is also suspected of being involved in the case, and they requested detention. Wang Yaoshi requested that she be allowed to find a guarantor to go out, so that she could be summoned easily at the next hearing. She requested that the case be postponed, etc. Judge Qian Wenji ordered the two defendants to be detained for further investigation in seven days and ordered Wang Yaoshi to be released on bail.

Midwife Cannot Escape Blame as Mother and Daughter Die Tragically

Midwife Abandons Patient in Critical Condition

Tang Guangyu, a resident of Zhenjiang living at No. 16, Lane 9, Yunnan Road, had a wife named Zhang, who was 38 years old. She was heavily pregnant and about to give birth. At around 7 AM the previous morning, she experienced severe labor pains. Her husband went to the residence of Wang He, a midwife living above the Yichang Incense Candle Shop near the Baxianqiao area of the French Concession, to request her services. After arriving at Tang's house, the midwife took Zhang's pulse and said that she would not give birth until the afternoon, instructing her husband to go out and buy necessary supplies. Unexpectedly, after Tang left, the midwife also returned home, leaving Zhang alone in the room without care. Around 9 AM, her labor pains intensified, and she gave birth to a daughter. When Tang returned home, he found his wife lying on the bed, struggling for breath, with blood everywhere. The child was already dead, and the midwife was nowhere to be seen, causing him great anxiety. In the afternoon, Zhang also died suddenly. Tang immediately reported the matter to the Lao Zha station of the police, who sent detectives to investigate and arrested the midwife. The bodies of the mother and daughter were sent to the forensic examination office on Avenue Petain. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court dispatched Prosecutor Guo Wei to the office to examine the bodies, open a case, and conduct an inquiry. The husband, Tang Guangyu, testified that he was 36 years old. When he went out to buy supplies, he specifically instructed the midwife not to leave because there was no one else at home. He was surprised that she had left before he returned, and he found the child dead and his wife suffering greatly. In the afternoon, she also died. He claimed that it was entirely the midwife's fault. Wang He testified that she was 48 years old and from Changshu. She said that she returned home to buy vegetables because no one was at her own home, and she asked the landlady to care for Zhang in her absence. After hearing the testimonies, Prosecutor Guo ruled that Zhang died from postpartum bleeding and the girl died from suffocation after birth. The midwife, Wang He, was suspected of committing a crime and should be prosecuted by the police and sent to the court for investigation. Zhang's body was released to her husband, Tang Guangyu, for burial.

Li Hongsheng, a Chinese detective from the Huishan Police Station, apprehended kidnapper Wang Jiang, a woman from Yangzhou, and Huang Wei on the Fujian steamer at the Osaka Wharf in Hongkou at 8 AM the day before yesterday. Subsequently, Wang Qiu, a woman from Jiangbei residing on Chang'an Road, reported that her biological son, Wang Koubao, was abducted from her doorstep several days ago and requested his return. Judge Wu briefly questioned the defendants and ordered them to be remanded in custody for further investigation. Wang Koubao was released to Wang Qiu, and Jin Dongquan was sent to the Women and Children Relief Association for care.

Regulations for River Steamers Towing Barges Approved by Ministry of Finance

Customs Announces Implementation Yesterday

Yesterday, Tang Hai'an, the superintendent of the Jianghai Customs in Shanghai, and Robert Bredon, the customs commissioner, jointly announced the implementation of the previously drafted regulations for Yangtze River steamers and electric boats towing civilian vessels, which had been approved by the Ministry of Finance. The announcement stated that the temporary regulations for Yangtze River steamers and electric boats towing vessels have now been approved by the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance for trial implementation. Therefore, the relevant regulations are copied below for the information of all merchants.

The regulations are as follows:

Temporary Regulations for Yangtze River Steamers and Electric Boats Towing Vessels

(Article 1) Steamers and electric boats operating in accordance with the Yangtze River Trade Regulations and having a long-term guarantee bond with the Customs may tow civilian cargo boats and barges from one treaty port to another, or from a treaty port to a permitted loading/unloading point, subject to Customs approval. However, towing civilian vessels above Yichang and towing civilian cargo boats and barges solely between loading/unloading points are prohibited.

(Article 2) In addition to the required documents, steamers and electric boats towing vessels must obtain a special towing permit from Customs, specifying the type and name of the steamer, the nationality and name of the shipping company, the number and type of vessels being towed, and the treaty ports or loading/unloading points where the towed vessels are loading or unloading cargo. When the steamer or electric boat arrives at the treaty port or loading/unloading point specified in the permit, it must present the permit to the Customs or other responsible authority, which will certify that the permit is for one-time use only. Upon arrival at the final treaty port, the permit must be returned to the Customs for cancellation. Steamers and electric boats towing vessels without a permit will be fined 750 yuan and the taxable goods on the towed vessels will be confiscated.

(Article 3) The manifest of the steamer or electric boat towing vessels must specify the cargo loaded on each towed vessel in detail. The cargo loaded on the towed vessels must be handled in accordance with the rules for vessel import inspection and documentation.

(Article 4) Cargoes loaded on vessels towed by steamers or electric boats from one treaty port to another, or from a treaty port to a loading/unloading point, must be declared to Customs. The assessment and handling of taxes will be carried out in the same way as ordinary cargo transported by steamer.

(Article 5) Steamers and electric boats towing vessels must report to each treaty port or loading/unloading point listed on the permit and submit the towed vessels for inspection. Failure to comply will result in the captain, owner, or agent of the steamer or electric boat being held solely or jointly liable. If the towed vessels and their cargo are being towed to a treaty port or loading/unloading point along the way, rather than to the final destination of the steamer or electric boat, the Customs or responsible authority at the intermediate port should clearly indicate this on the permit.

(Article 6) The number of vessels towed by a steamer or electric boat shall be reported to Customs for review and decision. The decision will be based on the engine horsepower of the steamer or electric boat, the availability of equipment for towing, and the ability to maintain safety in navigation, life, and property. If the steamer or electric boat violates this decision, obstructs navigation, or endangers life and property, the captain, owner, or agent of the steamer or electric boat will be fined up to 750 yuan. If an accident occurs, they will also be held legally responsible.

(Article 7) Steamers and electric boats towing vessels may not add vessels during the voyage without the formal permission of the Customs at a treaty port. Failure to comply will result in the captain, owner, or agent of the steamer or electric boat being fined up to 750 yuan and the taxable goods on the unauthorized towed vessels will be confiscated.

(Article 8) Steamers and electric boats towing vessels and the vessels they are towing must display navigation lights in accordance with the rules for preventing collisions at sea.

(Article 9) If a steamer or electric boat applies to tow vessels loaded with salt, Customs will not approve it without a formal document from the salt administration.

(Article 10) Steamers and electric boats towing vessels must comply with orders from Customs patrol boats to stop for inspection.

(Article 11) The crew of the cargo vessels towed by steamers or electric boats shall be limited to the number necessary for the management of the vessel, and passengers may not be carried.

(Article 12) Steamers and electric boats operating to Changsha and the vessels they are towing must comply with the special regulations for managing vessels in Changsha and Yuezhou during the low-water season in the Xiang River.

(Article 13) Steamers and electric boats towing civilian cargo boats and barges from a treaty port to various inland locations must comply with the regulations for vessels operating in inland ports.

(Article 14) These regulations may be amended as needed.

National Chamber of Commerce Requests Exemption of Stamp Tax for Small Transactions

The National Chamber of Commerce, based on a request from the Xiamen Chamber of Commerce, telegraphed the Ministry of Finance regarding the strict enforcement of stamp tax on small transactions by the local stamp tax bureau. This procedure not only makes transactions overly cumbersome but also places a heavy burden on small merchants. The telegram requested an exemption and uniform compliance from all stamp tax bureaus nationwide. The telegram reads as follows:

To the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing:

We have received a telegram from the Xiamen Chamber of Commerce stating that the local stamp tax bureau is enforcing stamp tax on small transactions too strictly. This procedure not only makes transactions overly cumbersome but also places a heavy burden on small merchants. It is requested that an exemption be granted and uniform compliance be sought from all stamp tax bureaus nationwide. After investigation, it has been found that small transactions have traditionally not involved invoices. When a market is busy, it is difficult for shops to issue invoices, and customers are often impatient. Some customers may even leave before the invoice is prepared. Moreover, small vendors of fish, meat, vegetables, and other goods are often illiterate and unable to issue invoices. If stamp duty is promoted and requires them to hire employees to handle this task, the small businesses might not be able to afford it. Therefore, we hereby telegraph to the Ministry to request that the Xiamen stamp tax bureau not force vendors to issue invoices and affix stamps for small transactions when customers do not require them, and that a circular be sent to all stamp tax bureaus nationwide to follow this procedure in order to alleviate the difficulties of merchants.

Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Chamber of Commerce Federation.

War Zone Work Research Association Calls for Donations of Comfort Items

The War Zone Work Research Association, organized by various sectors of society, has issued a letter to various circles of society, stating that frontline soldiers are fighting valiantly against the enemy and soliciting donations of medicines, clothing, shoes, and socks for the wounded, to be sent to the front lines to comfort the warriors fighting against the enemy. The letter states:

Respectfully, since the Japanese invasion has intensified, like a greedy boar or long serpent, they are advancing towards the interior. The pain of national subjugation is imminent. Waging war against the enemy relies on the efforts of the soldiers on the front lines, and providing supplies and comfort is the responsibility of the people in the rear. According to those who have just returned from inspecting the front lines, the troops fighting bravely to defend the country near the Great Wall are facing extreme difficulties, and there is an urgent need for medicines, clothing, underwear, cotton quilts, and shoes and socks. In addition to raising over 1,000 yuan to purchase medicines, there is still no source for clothing, underwear, cotton quilts, and shoes and socks. We know that you have a history of providing assistance and have a fervent enthusiasm for helping those in need. Therefore, we are sending this letter to request generous donations and to encourage your friends and relatives to donate as well. Each item will strengthen our ability to resist aggression. Please send the items to the following two locations by April 30th. Once a sufficient quantity has been collected, we will arrange for their safe delivery to the front lines. If you have difficulty with transportation, please notify us at any time, and we will send someone with a receipt to pick them up.

Addresses:

(1) Mr. Zheng Wenhan, China Vocational Education Society, Huanlong Road, French Concession (telephone 84817)

(2) Mr. Li Gongpu, Shen Bao Circulation Library, Nos. 345, Nanjing Road, Dalu Department Store (telephone 93321)

War Zone Work Research Association.

Reader Advisor

Collection of Letters Discussing the Question "Can I Return to the Countryside?" (17)

Letter from Mr. Lang Xian of Nanjing:

How can we launch a revolutionary national war under the current conditions?

Congratulations to Mr. Liu Simin for reading Mr. You's response to Mr. Xiong Sheng. I was just about to refute him when I received your first letter, Mr. Liu, which was uplifting. I thought you would be able to point out a correct and bright path forward. However, after reading your long letter for the second and third time, I was greatly disappointed! On the one hand, you acknowledge (the suffering of farmers, naturally is exorbitant taxes and levies… the exploitation of high interest rates… the forcing of opium cultivation by warlords and officials… farmers not owning their land…); and on the other hand, you believe that the masses throughout the country currently have (enthusiasm for a national war and an anti-imperialist war), that now is (the time to fight to the death with Japanese imperialists), and you expect (the masses to rise up and implement national armed mobilization…). Thus, your only solution to (the entire social problem of China) seems to be (armed resistance against Japan). This is the most fashionable argument now, but I, in my ignorance, am truly perplexed! Indeed, no one can deny that China is under the control of imperialism, but China has not yet become a colony directly ruled by imperialist countries. So how do they control us? What is the significance of the existence of feudal forces, warlords, local tyrants, and the comprador class? ... You say (the suffering of farmers, naturally is exorbitant taxes and levies…), so since the vast majority of farmers, who form the foundation of Chinese society, (can deeply feel their own suffering), they (know that local bullies, greedy clerks, and corrupt officials are their enemies). As for what imperialism is and what relationship they have with it, they are still completely clueless at this moment! When Rehe was about to fall, a Reuters reporter interviewed villagers in Miyun on the Pingre Highway behind the front lines, asking for their opinions on the Sino-Japanese War. They replied: (We haven't heard of any fighting there), which is the best proof. This is not surprising at all. They only feel that their suffering is given to them by warlords and local bullies. As for the imperialists behind these demons, except for the people in the Northeast, who have already fallen to the enemy, and the workers and clerks in large cities, where foreign influence directly reaches, they have no opportunity to recognize them, and propaganda alone cannot attract their attention. Mr. Liu, you (grew up half in the countryside), so you probably don't really not know this, right? Then your view is putting the cart before the horse.

Quarterly Reserve Report of the Four Banks Joint Treasury

Report No. 173

The Four Banks Joint Treasury is jointly established by the Yanye Bank, Jincheng Bank, Zhongnan Bank, and Dalu Bank, specializing in the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. In accordance with the treasury's issuance charter, the banknotes are issued with 100% reserves, with cash reserves of at least 60% and guarantee reserves of up to 40%. A weekly announcement is made after verification by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. The following is a copy of the 173rd announcement of the Shanghai Reserve Treasury on April 22, 1933.

Banknote Circulation: 18,341,737 yuan

Total Reserve: 18,341,737 yuan

Including:

Cash Reserve: 15,211,337 yuan

Guarantee Reserve: 3,130,400 yuan

According to the weather forecast from the Xujiahui Observatory at 4:30 PM yesterday, there is a moderate cyclone in the northeastern East China Sea and the Korean Peninsula. Air pressure is rising in the Yangtze River basin, and the weather is gradually improving. Along the coast of the country, the wind is light and shifting, with a possibility of heavy fog. Furthermore, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the local temperature was at its highest 69.1 and at its lowest 61.2. On the same day last year, it was at its highest 69.8 and at its lowest 44.6.

(18) Mr. Zhang Hailiang from this city wrote a letter asking Mr. Liu Simin what methods should be adopted to solve the problem of rural China? I have read in your column ("The Problem of Going to the Countryside") from when Mr. You Huaigao advised Mr. Xiong Sheng to return to the countryside, until today (the 17th), the letter from Mr. Liu Simin questioning Mr. You Huaigao and Mr. Zhu Tianqing, and it has stirred up some small opinions in me. I feel that you gentlemen have written thousands of words, discussing everything from the question of (can one return from the countryside) to the problems of the countryside, and even national crisis. From my foolish brain, I thought that this kind of discussion would definitely lead to a correct solution to the rural problem, or even a considerable solution to the national crisis, but reading through one article after another, I was disappointed! Perhaps other readers feel the same disappointment?

In this way, it may be possible to revitalize the countryside. My humble opinion is like this, what do the readers think?
